<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Simón Bolívar</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>

<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Liberator of South American countries</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"Bolívar" redirects here. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Bol%C3%ADvar_(disambiguation)" title="Bolívar (disambiguation)">Bolívar (disambiguation)</a> and <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar_(disambiguation)" title="Simón Bolívar (disambiguation)">Simón Bolívar (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">In this <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_name" title="Spanish name">Spanish name</a>, the first or paternal <a href="/wiki/Surname" title="Surname">surname</a> is <i> Bolívar</i> and the second or maternal family name is <i> Palacios</i>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

<p><b>Simón José Antonio de la Santísima Trinidad Bolívar y Palacios</b> (24 July 1783 – 17 December 1830) was a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Venezuelan_people" title="Venezuelan people">Venezuelan</a> military and political leader who led what are currently the countries of <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a>, <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a> to independence from the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a>. He is known colloquially as <i><a href="/wiki/Libertadores" title="Libertadores">El Libertador</a></i>, or the <i>Liberator of America</i>.
</p><p>Simón Bolívar was born in <a href="/wiki/Caracas" title="Caracas">Caracas</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_Venezuela" title="Captaincy General of Venezuela">Captaincy General of Venezuela</a> into a wealthy <a href="/wiki/Criollo_people" title="Criollo people">criollo</a> family. Before he turned ten, he lost both parents and lived in several households. Bolívar was educated abroad and lived in Spain, as was common for men of upper-class families in his day. While living in <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a> from 1800 to 1802, he was introduced to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enlightenment_philosophy" title="Enlightenment philosophy">Enlightenment philosophy</a> and met his future wife <a href="/wiki/Mar%C3%ADa_Teresa_Rodr%C3%ADguez_del_Toro_y_Alaysa" title="María Teresa Rodríguez del Toro y Alaysa">María Teresa Rodríguez del Toro y Alaysa</a>. After returning to Venezuela, in 1803 del Toro contracted <a href="/wiki/Yellow_fever" title="Yellow fever">yellow fever</a> and died. From 1803 to 1805, Bolívar embarked on a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_tour" title="Grand tour">grand tour</a> that ended in <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>, where he swore to end the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_America" title="Spanish America">Spanish rule in the Americas</a>. In 1807, Bolívar returned to Venezuela and proposed gaining Venezuelan independence to other wealthy creoles. When the Spanish authority in the Americas weakened due to <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_War" title="Peninsular War">Napoleon's Peninsular War</a>, Bolívar became a zealous combatant and politician in the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_American_wars_of_independence" title="Spanish American wars of independence">Spanish American wars of independence</a>.
</p><p>Bolívar began his military career in 1810 as a militia officer in the <a href="/wiki/Venezuelan_War_of_Independence" title="Venezuelan War of Independence">Venezuelan War of Independence</a>, fighting Spanish and more native <a href="/wiki/Royalist_(Spanish_American_independence)" title="Royalist (Spanish American independence)">Royalist</a> forces for the <a href="/wiki/First_Republic_of_Venezuela" title="First Republic of Venezuela">first</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_Republic_of_Venezuela" title="Second Republic of Venezuela">second</a> Venezuelan republics and the <a href="/wiki/United_Provinces_of_New_Granada" title="United Provinces of New Granada">United Provinces of New Granada</a>. After Spanish forces <a href="/wiki/Spanish_reconquest_of_New_Granada" title="Spanish reconquest of New Granada">subdued New Granada</a> in 1815, Bolívar was forced into exile in the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Haiti_(1806%E2%80%931820)" title="Republic of Haiti (1806–1820)">Republic of Haiti</a>, led by Haitian revolutionary <a href="/wiki/Alexandre_P%C3%A9tion" title="Alexandre Pétion">Alexandre Pétion</a>. Bolívar befriended Pétion and, after promising to abolish slavery in South America, received military support from Haiti. Returning to Venezuela, he established a <a href="/wiki/Third_Republic_of_Venezuela" title="Third Republic of Venezuela">third republic</a> in 1817 and then crossed the Andes in 1819 to <a href="/wiki/Bol%C3%ADvar%27s_campaign_to_liberate_New_Granada" title="Bolívar's campaign to liberate New Granada">liberate New Granada</a>. Bolívar and his allies defeated the Spanish in New Granada in 1819, Venezuela and Panama in 1821, Ecuador in 1822, Peru in 1824, and Bolivia in 1825. Venezuela, New Granada, Ecuador, and Panama were merged into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_Colombia" title="Republic of Colombia">Republic of Colombia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Gran_Colombia" title="Gran Colombia">Gran Colombia</a>), with Bolívar as president there and in Peru and Bolivia.
</p><p>In his final years, Bolívar became increasingly disillusioned with the South American republics, and distanced from them because of his centralist ideology. He was successively removed from his offices until, after a failed assassination attempt, he resigned the presidency of Colombia and died of <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a> in 1830. He is regarded as a <a href="/wiki/Father_of_the_Nation" title="Father of the Nation">national and cultural icon</a> throughout Latin America; the nations of Bolivia and Venezuela and their currencies are named after him. His legacy is diverse and far-reaching both within Latin America and beyond and he has been memorialized all over the world in the form of public art or street names and in popular culture.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life_and_family">Early life and family</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life and family">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Simón Bolívar was born on 24 July 1783 in <a href="/wiki/Caracas" title="Caracas">Caracas</a>, capital of the <a href="/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_Venezuela" title="Captaincy General of Venezuela">Captaincy General of Venezuela</a>, the fourth and youngest child of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Juan_Vicente_Bol%C3%ADvar_y_Ponte&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Juan Vicente Bolívar y Ponte (page does not exist)">Juan Vicente Bolívar y Ponte</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Juan_Vicente_Bol%C3%ADvar_y_Ponte" title="es:Juan Vicente Bolívar y Ponte">es</a>]</span> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mar%C3%ADa_de_la_Concepci%C3%B3n_Palacios_y_Blanco&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="María de la Concepción Palacios y Blanco (page does not exist)">María de la Concepción Palacios y Blanco</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mar%C3%ADa_de_la_Concepci%C3%B3n_Palacios_y_Blanco" title="es:María de la Concepción Palacios y Blanco">es</a>]</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196920,_22Lynch20062Langley20094Arana20136–8_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196920,_22Lynch20062Langley20094Arana20136–8-4">[3]</a></sup> He was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baptized" title="Baptized">baptized</a> as Simón José Antonio de la Santísma Trinidad Bolívar y Palacios on 30 July.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELangley20094_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELangley20094-5">[4]</a></sup> Simón was born into the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Bol%C3%ADvar_family&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Bolívar family (page does not exist)">Bolívar family</a>, one of the wealthiest and most prestigious <a href="/wiki/Criollo_people" title="Criollo people">criollo</a> families in the Spanish Americas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196920Langley20094Arana20137,_17_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196920Langley20094Arana20137,_17-6">[5]</a></sup> The first Bolívar to emigrate to the Americas was Simón de Bolívar, a <a href="/wiki/Basques" title="Basques">Basque</a> nobleman and notary official who arrived in <a href="/wiki/Santo_Domingo" title="Santo Domingo">Santo Domingo</a> in the mid-16th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196920Slattade_Grummond200310Arana20138–9_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196920Slattade_Grummond200310Arana20138–9-7">[6]</a></sup> In 1588–89, he joined the staff of <a href="/wiki/Diego_Osorio_Villegas" title="Diego Osorio Villegas">Diego Osorio Villegas</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Governor_of_Santo_Domingo" title="Governor of Santo Domingo">Governor of Santo Domingo</a>, when he was named <a href="/wiki/List_of_governors_of_Venezuela_Province" title="List of governors of Venezuela Province">Governor</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Venezuela_Province" title="Venezuela Province">Venezuela Province</a> and moved to Caracas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200310Arana20139_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200310Arana20139-8">[7]</a></sup> There, Simón de Bolívar's descendants would also serve in the colonial bureaucracy and marry into rich Caracas families.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196920Slattade_Grummond200310–11Langley20094_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196920Slattade_Grummond200310–11Langley20094-9">[8]</a></sup> By the time Simón Bolívar was born, the Bolívars owned property throughout Venezuela.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196920Lynch20064,_10Langley20094_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196920Lynch20064,_10Langley20094-10">[9]</a></sup>
</p><p>Simón Bolívar's childhood was described by British historian <a href="/wiki/John_Lynch_(historian)" title="John Lynch (historian)">John Lynch</a> as "at once privileged and deprived."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch20067_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch20067-11">[10]</a></sup> Juan Vicente died of tuberculosis on 19 January 1786,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200312Langley2009xixArana201321_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200312Langley2009xixArana201321-12">[11]</a></sup> and left María de la Concepción Palacios and her father, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Feliciano_Palacios_y_Sojo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Feliciano Palacios y Sojo (page does not exist)">Feliciano Palacios y Sojo</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feliciano_Palacios_de_Aguirre_y_Arizt%C3%ADa-Sojo_y_Gil_de_Arratia" title="es:Feliciano Palacios de Aguirre y Ariztía-Sojo y Gil de Arratia">es</a>]</span>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELangley20099Arana201318_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELangley20099Arana201318-13">[12]</a></sup> as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legal_guardians" title="Legal guardians">legal guardians</a> over the Bolívar children's inheritances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196923Langley20099Arana201318_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196923Langley20099Arana201318-14">[13]</a></sup> Those children – <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mar%C3%ADa_Antonia_Bol%C3%ADvar_Palacios&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="María Antonia Bolívar Palacios (page does not exist)">María Antonia</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mar%C3%ADa_Antonia_Bol%C3%ADvar_Palacios" title="es:María Antonia Bolívar Palacios">es</a>]</span> (born 1777), <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Juana_Bol%C3%ADvar_Palacios&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Juana Bolívar Palacios (page does not exist)">Juana</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Juana_Bol%C3%ADvar_Palacios" title="es:Juana Bolívar Palacios">es</a>]</span> (born 1779), <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Juan_Vicente_Bol%C3%ADvar_Palacios&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Juan Vicente Bolívar Palacios (page does not exist)">Juan Vicente</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Juan_Vicente_Bol%C3%ADvar_Palacios" title="es:Juan Vicente Bolívar Palacios">es</a>]</span> (born 1781), and Simón<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200311_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200311-15">[14]</a></sup> – were raised separately from each other and their mother, and, following colonial custom, by African <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/House_slaves" title="House slaves">house slaves</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196922–23_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196922–23-16">[15]</a></sup> Simón  was raised by a slave named <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Hip%C3%B3lita_Bol%C3%ADvar&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Hipólita Bolívar (page does not exist)">Hipólita</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hip%C3%B3lita_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="es:Hipólita Bolívar">es</a>]</span> whom he viewed as both a motherly and fatherly figure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196922–23Slattade_Grummond200311–12Lynch200616Arana20137–8,_22_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196922–23Slattade_Grummond200311–12Lynch200616Arana20137–8,_22-17">[16]</a></sup> On 6 July 1792,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200312Langley2009xix_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200312Langley2009xix-18">[17]</a></sup> María de la Concepción also died of tuberculosis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196923Langley20099Arana201324_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196923Langley20099Arana201324-19">[18]</a></sup> Believing that his family would inherit the Bolívars' wealth,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArana201325_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArana201325-20">[19]</a></sup> Feliciano Palacios arranged marriages for María Antonia and Juana and,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196923Slattade_Grummond200313Arana201324_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196923Slattade_Grummond200313Arana201324-21">[20]</a></sup> before dying on 5 December 1793,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200313_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200313-22">[21]</a></sup> assigned custody of Juan Vicente and Simón to his sons, Juan Félix Palacios and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Carlos_Palacios_y_Blanco&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Carlos Palacios y Blanco (page does not exist)">Carlos Palacios y Blanco</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carlos_Palacios_y_Blanco" title="es:Carlos Palacios y Blanco">es</a>]</span>, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196924Arana201325_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196924Arana201325-23">[22]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Education_and_first_journey_to_Europe.2C_1793.E2.80.931802"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Education_and_first_journey_to_Europe,_1793–1802">Education and first journey to Europe, 1793–1802</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Education and first journey to Europe, 1793–1802">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As a child, Bolívar was notoriously unruly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196923–24Langley20099Arana201322_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196923–24Langley20099Arana201322-24">[23]</a></sup> He came to loathe Carlos,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch200617_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch200617-25">[24]</a></sup> who had no interest in Bolívar other than his inheritance,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELangley20099Arana201325_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELangley20099Arana201325-26">[25]</a></sup> and neglected his studies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArana201325_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArana201325-20">[19]</a></sup> Even before Bolívar's mother died, he spent two years under the tutelage of the Venezuelan lawyer <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Jos%C3%A9_Sanz" title="Miguel José Sanz">Miguel José Sanz</a> at the direction of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Real_Audiencia_of_Caracas" title="Real Audiencia of Caracas"><i>Real Audiencia</i> of Caracas</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Audiencia_de_Caracas" title="es:Real Audiencia de Caracas">es</a>]</span>, the <a href="/wiki/Real_Audiencia" title="Real Audiencia">Spanish court of appeals</a> in Caracas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196923–24Langley20099Arana201322–23_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196923–24Langley20099Arana201322–23-27">[26]</a></sup> In 1793, Carlos Palacios enrolled Bolívar at <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Casa_de_Las_Primeras_Letras&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Casa de Las Primeras Letras (page does not exist)">a rudimentary primary school</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Casa_de_Las_Primeras_Letras" title="es:Casa de Las Primeras Letras">es</a>]</span> run by <a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Rodr%C3%ADguez" title="Simón Rodríguez">Simón Rodríguez</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch200617Arana201332_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch200617Arana201332-28">[27]</a></sup> In June 1795, Bolívar fled his uncle's custody for the house of Maria Antonia and her husband.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196925Slattade_Grummond200314Lynch200617Arana201332_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196925Slattade_Grummond200314Lynch200617Arana201332-29">[28]</a></sup> The couple sought formal recognition of his change of residence,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArana201332_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArana201332-30">[29]</a></sup> but the <i>Real Audiencia</i> decided the matter in favor of Palacios, who sent Simón to live with Rodríguez.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196925Lynch200617Arana201333_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196925Lynch200617Arana201333-31">[30]</a></sup>
</p><p>After two months there, Bolívar was moved at the direction of the <i>Real Audiencia</i> back to the Palacios family home.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196925Arana201334_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196925Arana201334-32">[31]</a></sup> Bolívar promised the <i>Real Audiencia</i> that he would focus on his education, and was subsequently taught full-time by Rodríguez and the Venezuelan intellectuals <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9s_Bello" title="Andrés Bello">Andrés Bello</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Francisco_de_And%C3%BAjar&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Francisco de Andújar (page does not exist)">Francisco de Andújar</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Francisco_de_And%C3%BAjar" title="es:Francisco de Andújar">es</a>]</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196924–25Lynch200616–17Arana201334–35_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196924–25Lynch200616–17Arana201334–35-33">[32]</a></sup> In 1797, Rodríguez's connection to <a href="/wiki/Gual_and_Espa%C3%B1a_conspiracy" title="Gual and España conspiracy">a pro-independence conspiracy</a> forced him to go into exile,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196927Lynch200617Arana201336–37_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196927Lynch200617Arana201336–37-34">[33]</a></sup> and Bolívar was enrolled in an honorary militia force. When he was commissioned as an officer after a year,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196927Slattade_Grummond200317Lynch200618Arana201337_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196927Slattade_Grummond200317Lynch200618Arana201337-35">[34]</a></sup> his uncles Carlos and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Esteban_Palacios_y_Blanco&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Esteban Palacios y Blanco (page does not exist)">Esteban Palacios y Blanco</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Esteban_Palacios_y_Blanco" title="es:Esteban Palacios y Blanco">es</a>]</span> decided to send Bolívar to join the latter in <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch200618Arana201337_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch200618Arana201337-36">[35]</a></sup> There, Esteban was friends with Queen <a href="/wiki/Maria_Luisa_of_Parma" title="Maria Luisa of Parma">Maria Luisa</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Favorite" title="Favorite">favorite</a>, Manuel Mallo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200317Arana201342_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200317Arana201342-37">[36]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar,_1800.jpg"><img alt="Miniature portrait of Bolívar in 1800" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="281" data-file-width="220" decoding="async" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar%2C_1800.jpg/130px-Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar%2C_1800.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar%2C_1800.jpg/195px-Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar%2C_1800.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/66/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar%2C_1800.jpg 2x" width="130"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar,_1800.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miniature_portrait" title="Miniature portrait">Miniature portrait</a> of Bolívar in 1800</div></div></div>
<p>On 19 January 1799, Bolívar boarded the Spanish warship <a href="/wiki/Spanish_ship_San_Ildefonso" title="Spanish ship San Ildefonso"><i>San Ildefonso</i></a> at the port of <a href="/wiki/La_Guaira" title="La Guaira">La Guaira</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196927Lynch200618Arana201338_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196927Lynch200618Arana201338-38">[37]</a></sup> bound for <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz" title="Cádiz">Cádiz</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArana201337_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArana201337-39">[38]</a></sup> The ship sailed first to <a href="/wiki/Veracruz_(city)" title="Veracruz (city)">Veracruz</a> to load Mexican silver for transit to Spain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200317–18Arana201339_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200317–18Arana201339-40">[39]</a></sup> The ship arrived on 2 February,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArana201339_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArana201339-41">[40]</a></sup> but was prevented from leaving for seven weeks by a British blockade of <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200318Arana201339_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200318Arana201339-42">[41]</a></sup> The <i>San Ildefonso</i> docked in <a href="/wiki/Santo%C3%B1a" title="Santoña">Santoña</a>, on the northern coast of Spain, in May 1799.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200318Lynch200618_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200318Lynch200618-43">[42]</a></sup> A little over a week later,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200318Arana201343_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200318Arana201343-44">[43]</a></sup> Bolívar arrived in Madrid and joined Esteban,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200318Lynch200619Arana201343_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200318Lynch200619Arana201343-45">[44]</a></sup> who found Bolívar to be "very ignorant".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196928Slattade_Grummond200318Langley200913Arana201344_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196928Slattade_Grummond200318Langley200913Arana201344-46">[45]</a></sup> Esteban asked Gerónimo Enrique de Uztáriz y Tovar, a Caracas native and government official, to educate Bolívar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArana201344_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArana201344-47">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECardozo_Uzcátegui201117–18_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECardozo_Uzcátegui201117–18-48">[47]</a></sup> Uztáriz accepted and Bolívar, who moved into his residence in February 1800,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECardozo_Uzcátegui201114,_19_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECardozo_Uzcátegui201114,_19-49">[48]</a></sup> was thoroughly educated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196928Langley200913Arana201344_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196928Langley200913Arana201344-50">[49]</a></sup>
</p><p>At the same time, Mallo fell out of the Queen's favor and <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Godoy" title="Manuel Godoy">Manuel Godoy</a>, her previous favorite, returned to power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200319Arana201346_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200319Arana201346-51">[50]</a></sup> As members of Mallo's faction at court, Esteban was arrested on pretense,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196930Slattade_Grummond200318Arana201346_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196930Slattade_Grummond200318Arana201346-52">[51]</a></sup> and Bolívar was banished from court following a public incident at the <a href="/wiki/Puerta_de_Toledo" title="Puerta de Toledo">Puerta de Toledo</a> over the wearing of diamonds without royal permission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196930–31Slattade_Grummond200319Langley200913_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196930–31Slattade_Grummond200319Langley200913-53">[52]</a></sup> Bolívar also at this time met <a href="/wiki/Mar%C3%ADa_Teresa_Rodr%C3%ADguez_del_Toro_y_Alaysa" title="María Teresa Rodríguez del Toro y Alaysa">María Teresa Rodríguez del Toro y Alaysa</a>, the daughter of another wealthy Caracas creole.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196930Slattade_Grummond200318–19Arana201346–47_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196930Slattade_Grummond200318–19Arana201346–47-54">[53]</a></sup> They were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Engaged" title="Engaged">engaged</a> in August 1800,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch200620_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch200620-55">[54]</a></sup> but were separated when the del Toros left Madrid for a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Summer_home" title="Summer home">summer home</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bilbao" title="Bilbao">Bilbao</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch200620Arana201347_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch200620Arana201347-56">[55]</a></sup> After Uztáriz left Madrid for a government assignment in <a href="/wiki/Teruel" title="Teruel">Teruel</a> in 1801,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch200620_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch200620-55">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECardozo_Uzcátegui201118_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECardozo_Uzcátegui201118-57">[56]</a></sup> Bolívar himself left for Bilbao and remained there when the del Toros returned to the capital in August 1801.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200319Arana201347_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200319Arana201347-58">[57]</a></sup> Early in 1802, Bolívar traveled to <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a> while he awaited permission to return to Madrid, which was granted in April.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196931Slattade_Grummond200319Lynch200620_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196931Slattade_Grummond200319Lynch200620-59">[58]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Return_to_Venezuela_and_second_journey_to_Europe.2C_1802.E2.80.931805"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Return_to_Venezuela_and_second_journey_to_Europe,_1802–1805">Return to Venezuela and second journey to Europe, 1802–1805</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Return to Venezuela and second journey to Europe, 1802–1805">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bolívar and del Toro, aged 18 and 21 respectively, were married in Madrid on 26 May 1802.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch200620Arana201348_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch200620Arana201348-60">[59]</a></sup> The couple boarded the <i>San Ildefonso</i> in <a href="/wiki/A_Coru%C3%B1a" title="A Coruña">A Coruña</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArana201348_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArana201348-61">[60]</a></sup> on 15 June and sailed for La Guaira, where they arrived on 12 July,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch200620_55-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch200620-55">[54]</a></sup> and settled in Caracas. There, del Toro fell ill and died of <a href="/wiki/Yellow_fever" title="Yellow fever">yellow fever</a> on 22 January 1803 and was buried in the Bolívar family crypt at <a href="/wiki/Caracas_Cathedral" title="Caracas Cathedral">Caracas Cathedral</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200319Lynch200620Arana201349–50_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200319Lynch200620Arana201349–50-62">[61]</a></sup> Bolívar was devastated by del Toro's death, and later told <a href="/wiki/Louis_Peru_de_Lacroix" title="Louis Peru de Lacroix">Louis Peru de Lacroix</a>, one of his generals and biographers, that he swore to never remarry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196931Slattade_Grummond200319–20Lynch200621Langley200914Arana201350–51_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196931Slattade_Grummond200319–20Lynch200621Langley200914Arana201350–51-63">[62]</a></sup> By July 1803,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArana201351_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArana201351-64">[63]</a></sup> Bolívar decided to leave Venezuela for Europe. He entrusted his estates to an agent and his brother and in October boarded a ship bound for Cádiz.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200319–20Lynch200622Arana201351_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200319–20Lynch200622Arana201351-65">[64]</a></sup>
</p><p>Bolívar arrived in Spain in December 1803, then traveled to Madrid to console his father-in-law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196933–34Slattade_Grummond200320Lynch200622Langley200915Arana201351–52_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196933–34Slattade_Grummond200320Lynch200622Langley200915Arana201351–52-66">[65]</a></sup> In March 1804,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArana201352_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArana201352-67">[66]</a></sup> Madrid ordered all non-residents in the city to leave to alleviate a bread shortage brought about by resumed hostilities with Britain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200320Langley200915_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200320Langley200915-68">[67]</a></sup> Over April, Bolívar and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Fernando_Rodr%C3%ADguez_del_Toro&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Fernando Rodríguez del Toro (page does not exist)">Fernando Rodríguez del Toro</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fernando_Rodr%C3%ADguez_del_Toro" title="es:Fernando Rodríguez del Toro">es</a>]</span>, a childhood friend and relative of his wife, made their way to Paris and arrived in time for <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a> to be proclaimed <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_the_French" title="Emperor of the French">Emperor of the French</a> on 18 May 1804.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200320Arana201352_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200320Arana201352-69">[68]</a></sup> They rented an apartment on the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Rue_Vivienne&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Rue Vivienne (page does not exist)">Rue Vivienne</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rue_Vivienne" title="fr:Rue Vivienne">fr</a>]</span> and met with other South Americans such as <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Carlos_de_Mont%C3%BAfar&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Carlos de Montúfar (page does not exist)">Carlos de Montúfar</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carlos_de_Mont%C3%BAfar" title="es:Carlos de Montúfar">es</a>]</span>, <a href="/wiki/Vicente_Rocafuerte" title="Vicente Rocafuerte">Vicente Rocafuerte</a>, and Simón Rodríguez, who joined Bolívar and del Toro in their apartment. Bolívar soon thereafter began a <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/dalliance" title="wiktionary:dalliance">dalliance</a> with the Countess Dervieu du Villars,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200321Lynch200623Arana201353–54_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200321Lynch200623Arana201353–54-70">[69]</a></sup> who hosted a <a href="/wiki/Salon_(gathering)" title="Salon (gathering)">salon</a> frequented by members of French <a href="/wiki/High_society_(social_class)" title="High society (social class)">high society</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch200623Arana201354_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch200623Arana201354-71">[70]</a></sup> It was likely at this salon that Bolívar met the naturalists <a href="/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt" title="Alexander von Humboldt">Alexander von Humboldt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aim%C3%A9_Bonpland" title="Aimé Bonpland">Aimé Bonpland</a>, who had traveled through much of <a href="/wiki/Spanish_America" title="Spanish America">Spanish America</a> from 1799 to 1804, and allegedly discussed Spanish American independence with them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196936–37Slattade_Grummond200321–22Lynch200623Langley200915Arana201354,_57–58_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196936–37Slattade_Grummond200321–22Lynch200623Langley200915Arana201354,_57–58-72">[71]</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1062260506">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%;max-width:100%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:.5em 1.4em .8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:.5em 0 .8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{overflow:hidden;position:relative;margin:.5em auto .8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft span,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright span{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox>blockquote{margin:0;padding:0;border-left:0;font-family:inherit;font-size:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:110%;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote>:first-child{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote:last-child>:last-child{margin-bottom:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" “ ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" ” ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .quote-title,.mw-parser-output .quotebox .quotebox-quote{display:block}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:640px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{width:100%!important;margin:0 0 .8em!important;float:none!important}}</style><div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:20%; ;">
<blockquote class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">
<p>I swear before you [...] that I will not rest body or soul until I have broken the chains binding us to the will of Spanish might!
</p>
</blockquote>
<p><cite class="right-aligned" style="">Simón Bolívar, 15 August 1805<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBushnell2003114Brown20094_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBushnell2003114Brown20094-73">[72]</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div>
<p>On 2 December 1804, <a href="/wiki/Coronation_of_Napoleon" title="Coronation of Napoleon">Napoleon crowned himself Emperor</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_de_Paris" title="Notre Dame de Paris">Notre Dame de Paris</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196937Slattade_Grummond200323Arana201358_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196937Slattade_Grummond200323Arana201358-74">[73]</a></sup> Though he remained awed by Napoleon, Bolívar was disgusted and,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196937–38Slattade_Grummond200323Langley200915Arana201358–59_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196937–38Slattade_Grummond200323Langley200915Arana201358–59-75">[74]</a></sup> in April 1805, left Paris with Rodríguez and del Toro on a <a href="/wiki/Grand_Tour" title="Grand Tour">Grand Tour</a> to <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200324Lynch200625Arana201361_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200324Lynch200625Arana201361-76">[75]</a></sup> Beginning in <a href="/wiki/Lyon" title="Lyon">Lyon</a>, they traveled to <a href="/wiki/Chamb%C3%A9ry" title="Chambéry">Chambéry</a>, where the philosopher <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rousseau" title="Rousseau">Rousseau</a> had <a href="/wiki/Les_Charmettes" title="Les Charmettes">once resided</a>, through the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Savoy_Alps" title="Savoy Alps">Savoy Alps</a>, and then to <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196941Slattade_Grummond200324Lynch200625Arana201361–62_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196941Slattade_Grummond200324Lynch200625Arana201361–62-77">[76]</a></sup> The trio arrived on 26 May 1805 and witnessed Napoleon's coronation as <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy_(Napoleonic)" title="Kingdom of Italy (Napoleonic)">King of Italy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200324Arana201362_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200324Arana201362-78">[77]</a></sup> From Milan, they traveled down the <a href="/wiki/Po_Valley" title="Po Valley">Po Valley</a> to <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">Venice</a>, then to <a href="/wiki/Florence" title="Florence">Florence</a>, and then finally <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196941Slattade_Grummond200324Lynch200626Arana201363_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196941Slattade_Grummond200324Lynch200626Arana201363-79">[78]</a></sup> where Bolívar met among others <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_VII" title="Pope Pius VII">Pope Pius VII</a>, the French writer <a href="/wiki/Germaine_de_Sta%C3%ABl" title="Germaine de Staël">Germaine de Staël</a>, and Humboldt again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196941–42Arana201363,_65_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196941–42Arana201363,_65-80">[79]</a></sup> Rome's sites and history excited Bolívar. On 18 August 1805, he, del Toro, and Rodríguez traveled to the <a href="/wiki/Mons_Sacer" title="Mons Sacer">Mons Sacer</a>, where <a href="/wiki/First_secessio_plebis" title="First secessio plebis">the plebs had seceded from Rome</a>, Bolívar swore to end Spanish rule in the Americas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200324Lynch200626Arana201365–66_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200324Lynch200626Arana201365–66-81">[80]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_and_military_career">Political and military career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Political and military career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_career_of_Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Military career of Simón Bolívar">Military career of Simón Bolívar</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Francisco_de_Miranda_by_Tovar_y_Tovar.jpg"><img alt="Portrait of Francisco de Miranda" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="297" decoding="async" height="229" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Francisco_de_Miranda_by_Tovar_y_Tovar.jpg/170px-Francisco_de_Miranda_by_Tovar_y_Tovar.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Francisco_de_Miranda_by_Tovar_y_Tovar.jpg/255px-Francisco_de_Miranda_by_Tovar_y_Tovar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b3/Francisco_de_Miranda_by_Tovar_y_Tovar.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Francisco_de_Miranda_by_Tovar_y_Tovar.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Francisco_de_Miranda" title="Francisco de Miranda">Francisco de Miranda</a>, portrait by <a href="/wiki/Mart%C3%ADn_Tovar_y_Tovar" title="Martín Tovar y Tovar">Martín Tovar y Tovar</a></div></div></div>
<p>By April 1806, Bolívar had returned to Paris and desired passage to Venezuela,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch200627_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch200627-82">[81]</a></sup> where Venezuelan revolutionary <a href="/wiki/Francisco_de_Miranda" title="Francisco de Miranda">Francisco de Miranda</a> had just attempted an invasion with American volunteers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196955–56Slattade_Grummond200330Lynch200639Arana201370_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196955–56Slattade_Grummond200330Lynch200639Arana201370-83">[82]</a></sup> British <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Control_of_the_seas" title="Control of the seas">control of the seas</a> resulting from the 1805 <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Trafalgar" title="Battle of Trafalgar">Battle of Trafalgar</a>, however, obliged Bolívar to board an American ship in <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a> in October 1806. Bolívar arrived in <a href="/wiki/Charleston,_South_Carolina" title="Charleston, South Carolina">Charleston, South Carolina</a>, in January 1807,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200325Arana201371_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200325Arana201371-84">[83]</a></sup> and from there traveled to <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200325Lynch200639Arana201372_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200325Lynch200639Arana201372-85">[84]</a></sup> After six months in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELangley200918_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELangley200918-86">[85]</a></sup> Bolívar returned to Philadelphia and sailed for Venezuela, where he arrived in June 1807. He began to meet with other creole elites to discuss independence from Spain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200326Arana201377_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200326Arana201377-87">[86]</a></sup> Finding himself to be far more radical than the rest of Caracas high society,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200333–34Lynch200641Arana201380_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200333–34Lynch200641Arana201380-88">[87]</a></sup> however, Bolívar occupied himself with a property dispute with a neighbor, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Antonio_Nicol%C3%A1s_Brice%C3%B1o&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Antonio Nicolás Briceño (page does not exist)">Antonio Nicolás Briceño</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antonio_Nicol%C3%A1s_Brice%C3%B1o" title="es:Antonio Nicolás Briceño">es</a>]</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch200641Arana201377,_81_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch200641Arana201377,_81-89">[88]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1807–08, Napoleon <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_War" title="Peninsular War">invaded the Iberian peninsula</a> and <a href="/wiki/Abdications_of_Bayonne" title="Abdications of Bayonne">replaced the rulers of Spain</a> with <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Bonaparte" title="Joseph Bonaparte">his brother</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196961–62Slattade_Grummond200326–27Lynch200644Arana201377–78_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196961–62Slattade_Grummond200326–27Lynch200644Arana201377–78-90">[89]</a></sup> This news arrived in Venezuela in July 1808.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200331–32Lynch200645Arana201379_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200331–32Lynch200645Arana201379-91">[90]</a></sup> Napoleonic rule was rejected and Venezuelan creoles, though still loyal to <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_VII_of_Spain" title="Ferdinand VII of Spain">Ferdinand VII of Spain</a>, sought to form their own local government in place of the existing Spanish government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch200645–46Arana201379–80_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch200645–46Arana201379–80-92">[91]</a></sup> On 24 November 1808, a group of creoles presented a petition demanding an independent government to <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Juan_de_Casas&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Juan de Casas (page does not exist)">Juan de Casas</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Juan_de_Casas" title="es:Juan de Casas">es</a>]</span>, the Captain-General of Venezuela, and were arrested.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200333–34Lynch200646–47_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200333–34Lynch200646–47-93">[92]</a></sup> Bolívar, who did not sign the petition, was not arrested but was warned to cease hosting or attending seditious meetings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196965–66Lynch200646Arana201381_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196965–66Lynch200646Arana201381-94">[93]</a></sup> In May 1809, Casas was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Vicente_Empar%C3%A1n" title="Vicente Emparán">Vicente Emparán</a> and his staff, which included Fernando Rodríguez del Toro. Emparán's government, while friendlier to the creoles and connected to some of the opposition leaders,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200335Lynch200647Arana201382_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200335Lynch200647Arana201382-95">[94]</a></sup> was also resisted by the creoles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArana201383_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArana201383-96">[95]</a></sup>
</p><p>By February 1810, French victories in Spain prompted the dissolution of <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Central_Junta" title="Supreme Central Junta">the anti-French Spanish government</a> in favor of a five-man <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Regency_council" title="Regency council">regency council</a> for Ferdinand VII.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200335Lynch200647Arana201383–84_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200335Lynch200647Arana201383–84-97">[96]</a></sup> This news, and two delegates that included Carlos de Montúfar, arrived in Venezuela on 17 April 1810.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196967Arana201384_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196967Arana201384-98">[97]</a></sup> Two days later, the creoles succeeded in deposing and then expelling Emparán,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196968–69Slattade_Grummond200336–37Arana201384–86_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196968–69Slattade_Grummond200336–37Arana201384–86-99">[98]</a></sup> and created the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Junta" title="Supreme Junta">Supreme Junta of Caracas</a>, independent from the Spanish regency but not Ferdinand VII.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch200648Arana201386_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch200648Arana201386-100">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane201485_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane201485-101">[100]</a></sup> Absent from Caracas for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coup" title="Coup">coup</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200338Lynch200648_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200338Lynch200648-102">[101]</a></sup> the Bolívar brothers returned to the city and offered their services to the Supreme Junta as diplomats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200338Lynch200648Arana201387_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200338Lynch200648Arana201387-103">[102]</a></sup> In May 1810, Juan Vicente was sent to the United States to buy weapons,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200338_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200338-104">[103]</a></sup> while Simón secured a place in a diplomatic mission to <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">Great Britain</a> with the lawyer <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Luis_L%C3%B3pez_M%C3%A9ndez&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Luis López Méndez (page does not exist)">Luis López Méndez</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luis_L%C3%B3pez_M%C3%A9ndez" title="es:Luis López Méndez">es</a>]</span> and Andrés Bello by paying for the mission. The trio boarded a British warship, <a href="/wiki/French_brig_Oreste_(1805)" title="French brig Oreste (1805)">HMS <i>Wellington</i></a>, in June 1810 and arrived at <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth" title="Portsmouth">Portsmouth</a> on 10 July 1810.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196972–73Slattade_Grummond200338Lynch200648–49Langley200928Arana201387–88_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196972–73Slattade_Grummond200338Lynch200648–49Langley200928Arana201387–88-105">[104]</a></sup>
</p><p>The three delegates first met Miranda at his London residence, despite instructions from the Supreme Junta to avoid him, and thereafter received the benefit of his connections and consultation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch200649–50Arana201392_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch200649–50Arana201392-106">[105]</a></sup> On 16 July 1810, the Venezuelan delegation met the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_foreign_secretary" title="British foreign secretary">British foreign secretary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Wellesley,_1st_Marquess_Wellesley" title="Richard Wellesley, 1st Marquess Wellesley">Richard Wellesley</a>, at <a href="/wiki/Apsley_House" title="Apsley House">his residence</a>. Led by Bolívar, the Venezuelans argued in favor of Venezuelan independence. Wellesley stated that it was intolerable for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglo-Spanish_relations" title="Anglo-Spanish relations">Anglo-Spanish relations</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200339–40Lynch200651–52Arana201388–90_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200339–40Lynch200651–52Arana201388–90-107">[106]</a></sup> and moreover was using his talks with the Venezuelans to secure access to Spanish American markets for British merchants from the Spanish regency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196973–74Slattade_Grummond200341Arana201388_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196973–74Slattade_Grummond200341Arana201388-108">[107]</a></sup> Subsequent meetings produced no recognition or concrete support from Britain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196977Slattade_Grummond200340Lynch200652–53_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196977Slattade_Grummond200340Lynch200652–53-109">[108]</a></sup> Finding that he had many shared beliefs with Miranda, however, Bolívar convinced him to come back to Venezuela.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch200650Langley200930–31Arana201393–94_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch200650Langley200930–31Arana201393–94-110">[109]</a></sup> On 22 September 1810,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch200653Arana201395_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch200653Arana201395-111">[110]</a></sup> Bolívar left for Venezuela aboard <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=HMS_Sapphire_(1806)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="HMS Sapphire (1806) (page does not exist)">HMS <i>Sapphire</i></a> while López and Bello remained in London as diplomats,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200341Langley200931Arana201395_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200341Langley200931Arana201395-112">[111]</a></sup> and arrived in La Guaira on 5 December.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200341Lynch200653Arana201395_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200341Lynch200653Arana201395-113">[112]</a></sup> Miranda, whose return to Venezuela the British government did not desire but could not prevent,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196980–81Slattade_Grummond200341Lynch200653–54_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196980–81Slattade_Grummond200341Lynch200653–54-114">[113]</a></sup> arrived in La Guaira later in December.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200341–42Lynch200654Arana201396–97_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200341–42Lynch200654Arana201396–97-115">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[b]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Venezuela.2C_1811.E2.80.931812"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Venezuela,_1811–1812">Venezuela, 1811–1812</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Venezuela, 1811–1812">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/First_Republic_of_Venezuela" title="First Republic of Venezuela">First Republic of Venezuela</a></div>
<p>While Bolívar was in England, the Supreme Junta passed <a href="/wiki/Liberalism" title="Liberalism">liberal</a> economic reforms<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch200654Langley200931_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch200654Langley200931-122">[120]</a></sup> and began to hold elections for representatives to a congress to be held in Caracas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane201487_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane201487-123">[121]</a></sup> It had also alienated Caracas from the Venezuelan provinces of <a href="/wiki/Coro_Province" title="Coro Province">Coro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maracaibo_Province_(Spanish_Empire)" title="Maracaibo Province (Spanish Empire)">Maracaibo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Guayana_Province" title="Guayana Province">Guayana</a>, which professed loyalty to the regency council,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196983Langley200931_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196983Langley200931-124">[122]</a></sup> and began hostilities with them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196984Langley200931_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196984Langley200931-125">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane201487–88_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane201487–88-126">[124]</a></sup> Helping to create the <a href="/wiki/Patriotic_Society_(Venezuela)" title="Patriotic Society (Venezuela)">Patriotic Society</a>, Bolívar and Miranda campaigned for and secured the latter's election to the congress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200346Arana201397_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200346Arana201397-127">[125]</a></sup> The congress first met on 2 March 1811 and reaffirmed Caracas's allegiance to Ferdinand VII.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196986Slattade_Grummond200346_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196986Slattade_Grummond200346-128">[126]</a></sup> After it was discovered that one of the men leading the congress was a Spanish agent who had escaped with military documents, however,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArana2013100_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArana2013100-129">[127]</a></sup> discourse – which Bolívar was prominent in – changed decidedly in favor of independence over 3 and 4 July.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196987–88Slattade_Grummond200347Lynch200655Langley200933Arana2013100–01_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196987–88Slattade_Grummond200347Lynch200655Langley200933Arana2013100–01-130">[128]</a></sup> Finally, on 5 July, after a near-unanimous vote, the congress <a href="/wiki/Venezuelan_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Venezuelan Declaration of Independence">declared Venezuela's independence</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196988Slattade_Grummond200347Arana2013101_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196988Slattade_Grummond200347Arana2013101-131">[129]</a></sup>
</p><p>The declaration of independence created a republic with a weak base of support and enemies in conservative whites, disenfranchised people of color, and already hostile Venezuelan provinces, which received troops and supplies from the <a href="/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Captaincy General of Puerto Rico">Captaincy-Generals of Puerto Rico</a> and <a href="/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_Cuba" title="Captaincy General of Cuba">Cuba</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane201488–91_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane201488–91-132">[130]</a></sup> On 13 July 1811, the republic raised militias to fight the pro-Spanish <a href="/wiki/Royalist_(Spanish_American_independence)" title="Royalist (Spanish American independence)">Royalists</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch200656_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch200656-133">[131]</a></sup> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Francisco_Rodr%C3%ADguez_del_Toro&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Francisco Rodríguez del Toro (page does not exist)">Francisco Rodríguez del Toro</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Francisco_Rodr%C3%ADguez_del_Toro" title="es:Francisco Rodríguez del Toro">es</a>]</span>, the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Marquis_of_Toro&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Marquis of Toro (page does not exist)">Marquis of Toro</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marquesado_del_Toro" title="es:Marquesado del Toro">es</a>]</span> was appointed to command the Republican forces,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArana201399–100_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArana201399–100-134">[132]</a></sup> which opened a breach between Bolívar and Miranda as Bolívar and del Toro were friends.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch200658Arana2013100_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch200658Arana2013100-135">[133]</a></sup> After he failed to suppress a Royalist uprising in the city of <a href="/wiki/Valencia,_Venezuela" title="Valencia, Venezuela">Valencia</a> later in July,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196991Arana2013104_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196991Arana2013104-136">[134]</a></sup> Miranda replaced del Toro and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia_campaign&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Valencia campaign (page does not exist)">recaptured Valencia</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Campa%C3%B1a_de_Valencia" title="es:Campaña de Valencia">es</a>]</span> on 13 August.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane201491_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane201491-137">[135]</a></sup> As a condition of assuming command of the Republican forces, Miranda had Bolívar removed from his command of a militia unit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196991Slattade_Grummond200348Langley200934Langley200934Arana2013104_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196991Slattade_Grummond200348Langley200934Langley200934Arana2013104-138">[136]</a></sup> Bolívar nonetheless fought in the Valencia campaign as part of del Toro's militia<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196992Slattade_Grummond200348,_52Lynch200658Arana2013104–05_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196992Slattade_Grummond200348,_52Lynch200658Arana2013104–05-139">[137]</a></sup> and was selected by Miranda to bring news of its recapture to Caracas,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196992Arana2013105_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196992Arana2013105-140">[138]</a></sup> where he fruitlessly argued for more punitive and forceful campaigning against the Royalists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196993Arana2013105–06_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196993Arana2013105–06-141">[139]</a></sup> On 21 December, the congress ratified the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Federal_Constitution_of_the_States_of_Venezuela_of_1811&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Federal Constitution of the States of Venezuela of 1811 (page does not exist)">Constitution of 1811</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constituci%C3%B3n_Federal_de_los_Estados_de_Venezuela_de_1811" title="es:Constitución Federal de los Estados de Venezuela de 1811">es</a>]</span>. The decentralized government it constructed dismayed Bolívar and Miranda, who desired a <a href="/wiki/Centralized_government" title="Centralized government">centralized government</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196993–94Slattade_Grummond200354_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196993–94Slattade_Grummond200354-142">[140]</a></sup>
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1062260506" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:300px; ;">
<blockquote class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">
<p>I left my house for the Cathedral [...] and the earth began to shake with a huge roar. [...] I saw the church of San Jacinto collapse on its own foundations. [...] I climbed over the ruins and entered, and I immediately saw about forty persons dead or dying under the rubble. I climbed out again and I shall never forget that moment. On the top of the ruins I found Don Simón Bolívar [...]. He saw me and [said], "We will fight nature itself if it opposes us, and force it to obey."
</p>
</blockquote>
<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">Royalist historian <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Domingo_D%C3%ADaz&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="José Domingo Díaz (page does not exist)">José Domingo Díaz</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Domingo_D%C3%ADaz" title="es:José Domingo Díaz">es</a>]</span>, quoted by <a href="/wiki/John_Lynch_(historian)" title="John Lynch (historian)">John Lynch</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch20061_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch20061-143">[141]</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div>
<p>Beginning in November 1811, Royalist forces began pushing back the Republicans on from the north and east.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane201491–92_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane201491–92-144">[142]</a></sup> Then, on 26 March 1812, <a href="/wiki/1812_Caracas_earthquake" title="1812 Caracas earthquake">a powerful earthquake struck Venezuela</a>, devastating areas under Republican control; Caracas itself was almost totally destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200355Lynch200659Langley200935–36Arana2013107–09_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200355Lynch200659Langley200935–36Arana2013107–09-145">[143]</a></sup> Bolívar, who was still in the area of Caracas,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196996_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196996-146">[144]</a></sup> rushed into the city to participate in the rescue of survivors and exhumation of the dead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArana2013108–09_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArana2013108–09-147">[145]</a></sup> The earthquake also destroyed public support for the republic, as Royalists and Republicans alike believed it to have been <a href="/wiki/Divine_retribution" title="Divine retribution">divine retribution</a> for declaring independence from Spain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196995–96Slattade_Grummond200356Lynch200659Arana2013109–10_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196995–96Slattade_Grummond200356Lynch200659Arana2013109–10-148">[146]</a></sup> By April, a Royalist army under the Spanish naval officer <a href="/wiki/Juan_Domingo_de_Monteverde" title="Juan Domingo de Monteverde">Juan Domingo de Monteverde</a> overran western Venezuela. Miranda,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200357_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200357-149">[147]</a></sup> retreating east with a disintegrating army,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane201493_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane201493-150">[148]</a></sup> ordered Bolívar to assume command of the coastal city of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Cabello" title="Puerto Cabello">Puerto Cabello</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Felipe_Castle" title="San Felipe Castle">its fortress</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196997–98Lynch200660Arana2013112_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196997–98Lynch200660Arana2013112-151">[149]</a></sup> which contained Royalist prisoners and most of the republic's remaining arms and ammunition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200357Arana2013112_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200357Arana2013112-152">[150]</a></sup>
</p><p>Bolívar arrived at Puerto Cabello on 4 May 1812.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200357Lynch200660Arana2013112_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200357Lynch200660Arana2013112-153">[151]</a></sup> On 30 June, a Royalist officer of the fort's garrison released its prisoners, armed them, and turned its cannons on Puerto Cabello.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane201493_150-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane201493-150">[148]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969100Slattade_Grummond200358Arana2013114–15_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969100Slattade_Grummond200358Arana2013114–15-154">[152]</a></sup> Weakened by further shelling, defections, and lack of supplies, Bolívar and his remaining troops fled for La Guaira on 6 July.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969101Slattade_Grummond200358–59Arana2013_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969101Slattade_Grummond200358–59Arana2013-155">[153]</a></sup> Believing the republic to be doomed,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane201493_150-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane201493-150">[148]</a></sup> Miranda decided to capitulate,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969103Slattade_Grummond200363Arana2013118_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969103Slattade_Grummond200363Arana2013118-156">[154]</a></sup> shocking Bolívar and other Republican officers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200364Lynch200661Arana2013119_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200364Lynch200661Arana2013119-157">[155]</a></sup> After formally surrendering his command to Monteverde on 25 July,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch200661Arana2013118_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch200661Arana2013118-158">[156]</a></sup> Miranda made his way to La Guaira, where a group of conspirators that included Bolívar arrested and imprisoned Miranda on 30 July on charges of treason.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969103–04Slattade_Grummond200364–65Lynch200661–62Arana2013120–22_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969103–04Slattade_Grummond200364–65Lynch200661–62Arana2013120–22-159">[157]</a></sup> La Guaira declared for the Royalists the next day and closed its port on Monteverde's orders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969104–05Lynch200662Arana2013122_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969104–05Lynch200662Arana2013122-160">[158]</a></sup> Miranda, still incarcerated, was taken into Spanish custody and moved to a prison in Cádiz, where he died on 16 July 1816.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969105Langley200938_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969105Langley200938-161">[159]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="New_Granada_and_Venezuela.2C_1812.E2.80.931815"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Granada_and_Venezuela,_1812–1815">New Granada and Venezuela, 1812–1815</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: New Granada and Venezuela, 1812–1815">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bolívar escaped La Guaira early on 31 July 1812 and rode to Caracas,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969105Arana2013122_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969105Arana2013122-162">[160]</a></sup> where he hid from arrest in the home of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Esteban_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Le%C3%B3n&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Esteban Fernández de León (page does not exist)">Esteban Fernández de León</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Esteban_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Le%C3%B3n" title="es:Esteban Fernández de León">es</a>]</span>, the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Marquis_de_Casa_Le%C3%B3n&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Marquis de Casa León (page does not exist)">Marquis de Casa León</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marquesado_de_Casa_Le%C3%B3n" title="es:Marquesado de Casa León">es</a>]</span>. Bolívar and Casa León convinced Francisco Iturbe, a friend of the Bolívar family and of Monteverde, to intercede on Bolívar's behalf and secure escape from Venezuela for him. Iturbe persuaded Monteverde to issue Bolívar a passport for his role in Miranda's arrest,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969105–06Slattade_Grummond200367Lynch200662–63Arana2013124–26_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969105–06Slattade_Grummond200367Lynch200662–63Arana2013124–26-163">[161]</a></sup> and on 27 August he sailed for Curaçao. He and his uncles <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Jos%C3%A9_Ribas" title="Francisco José Ribas">Francisco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_F%C3%A9lix_Ribas" title="José Félix Ribas">José Félix Ribas</a> arrived on 1 September. Late in October, the exiles arranged for passage to the city of <a href="/wiki/Cartagena,_Colombia" title="Cartagena, Colombia">Cartagena</a> in <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_New_Granada" title="Viceroyalty of New Granada">New Granada</a> to offer their services to the <a href="/wiki/United_Provinces_of_New_Granada" title="United Provinces of New Granada">United Provinces of New Granada</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200367Langley200942Arana2013126–28_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200367Langley200942Arana2013126–28-164">[162]</a></sup> They arrived in November and were welcomed by <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Torices" title="Manuel Rodríguez Torices">Manuel Rodríguez Torices</a>, president of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Free_State_of_Cartagena&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Free State of Cartagena (page does not exist)">Free State of Cartagena</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Estado_Libre_de_Cartagena" title="es:Estado Libre de Cartagena">es</a>]</span>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969107,_112Arana2013128_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969107,_112Arana2013128-165">[163]</a></sup> who instructed his commanding general, <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Labatut" title="Pierre Labatut">Pierre Labatut</a>, to give Bolívar a military command. Labatut, a former partisan of Miranda, begrudgingly obliged and on 1 December 1812<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArana2013129_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArana2013129-166">[164]</a></sup> placed Bolívar in command of the 70-man garrison of a town on the lower <a href="/wiki/Magdalena_River" title="Magdalena River">Magdalena River</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200371Arana2013129,_132_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200371Arana2013129,_132-167">[165]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:British_exploits_in_South_America;_a_history_of_British_activities_in_exploration,_military_adventure,_diplomacy,_science,_and_trade,_in_Latin_American_(1917)_(14596816669).jpg"><img alt="Engraving of Bolívar" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2002" data-file-width="1602" decoding="async" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/British_exploits_in_South_America%3B_a_history_of_British_activities_in_exploration%2C_military_adventure%2C_diplomacy%2C_science%2C_and_trade%2C_in_Latin_American_%281917%29_%2814596816669%29.jpg/170px-thumbnail.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/British_exploits_in_South_America%3B_a_history_of_British_activities_in_exploration%2C_military_adventure%2C_diplomacy%2C_science%2C_and_trade%2C_in_Latin_American_%281917%29_%2814596816669%29.jpg/255px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/British_exploits_in_South_America%3B_a_history_of_British_activities_in_exploration%2C_military_adventure%2C_diplomacy%2C_science%2C_and_trade%2C_in_Latin_American_%281917%29_%2814596816669%29.jpg/340px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:British_exploits_in_South_America;_a_history_of_British_activities_in_exploration,_military_adventure,_diplomacy,_science,_and_trade,_in_Latin_American_(1917)_(14596816669).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1917 engraving of Bolívar</div></div></div>
<p>While en route to his posting, Bolívar issued the <a href="/wiki/Cartagena_Manifesto" title="Cartagena Manifesto">Cartagena Manifesto</a>, outlining what he believed to be the causes of the Venezuelan republic's defeat and his political program.
