In particular, Bolívar called for the disparate New Granadan republics to help him invade Venezuela to prevent a Royalist invasion of New Granada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969113–115Slattade_Grummond200370Lynch200666–68Arana2013130–31_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969113–115Slattade_Grummond200370Lynch200666–68Arana2013130–31-168">[166]</a></sup> Bolívar arrived on the Magdalena River on 21 December and,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969116_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969116-169">[167]</a></sup> in spite of orders from Labatut to not act without his direction,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969116Lynch200669Arana2013131–32_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969116Lynch200669Arana2013131–32-170">[168]</a></sup> launched <a href="/wiki/Magdalena_campaign" title="Magdalena campaign">an offensive</a> that secured control of the Magdalena River by 8 January 1813.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969116–17Slattade_Grummond200371–72Lynch200669–70Arana2013132–33_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969116–17Slattade_Grummond200371–72Lynch200669–70Arana2013132–33-171">[169]</a></sup> In February, he joined forces with Republican colonel <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Manuel_del_Castillo_y_Rada&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Manuel del Castillo y Rada (page does not exist)">Manuel del Castillo y Rada</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manuel_del_Castillo_y_Rada" title="es:Manuel del Castillo y Rada">es</a>]</span>, who requested Bolívar's assistance with stopping a Royalist advance into New Granada from Venezuela, and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_C%C3%BAcuta" title="Battle of Cúcuta">captured</a> the city of <a href="/wiki/C%C3%BAcuta" title="Cúcuta">Cúcuta</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969118–19Slattade_Grummond200372–73Arana2013136–38_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969118–19Slattade_Grummond200372–73Arana2013136–38-172">[170]</a></sup>
</p><p>In early March 1813, Bolívar set up his headquarters in Cúcuta and sent José Félix Ribas to request permission to invade Venezuela.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200373–74Lynch200670_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200373–74Lynch200670-173">[171]</a></sup> Though rewarded with honorary citizenship in New Granada and a promotion to the rank of <a href="/wiki/Brigadier_general" title="Brigadier general">brigadier general</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969119Slattade_Grummond200374Arana2013138_174-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969119Slattade_Grummond200374Arana2013138-174">[172]</a></sup> that permission did not come until 7 May because of del Castillo's opposition to the invasion. When a limited invasion was permitted, Castillo resigned his command and was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Francisco_de_Paula_Santander" title="Francisco de Paula Santander">Francisco de Paula Santander</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969119–20Slattade_Grummond200374–76Lynch200670–71Arana2013138–39_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969119–20Slattade_Grummond200374–76Lynch200670–71Arana2013138–39-175">[173]</a></sup> On 14 May, Bolívar launched the <a href="/wiki/Admirable_Campaign" title="Admirable Campaign">Admirable Campaign</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200375_176-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200375-176">[174]</a></sup> in which he issued the <a href="/wiki/Decree_of_War_to_the_Death" title="Decree of War to the Death">Decree of War to the Death</a>, ordering the death of all Spaniards in South America not actively aiding his forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969124Slattade_Grummond200377Lynch200673Langley200946Arana2013142–43_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969124Slattade_Grummond200377Lynch200673Langley200946Arana2013142–43-177">[175]</a></sup> Within six months, Bolívar pushed all the way to Caracas,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014115_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014115-178">[176]</a></sup> which he entered and paraded through on 6 August,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969129Slattade_Grummond200375Lynch200675Arana2013146_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969129Slattade_Grummond200375Lynch200675Arana2013146-179">[177]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014120_180-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014120-180">[178]</a></sup> and then defeated Monteverde near Puerto Cabello and drove him out of Venezuela in October.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200382–84Lynch200684_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200382–84Lynch200684-181">[179]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014123_182-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014123-182">[180]</a></sup> Bolívar returned to Caracas on 14 October and was named "The Liberator" (<i>El Libertador</i>) by its town council,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200384–85Lynch200679_183-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200384–85Lynch200679-183">[181]</a></sup> a title first given to him by the citizens of the Venezuelan town of <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A9rida,_M%C3%A9rida" title="Mérida, Mérida">Mérida</a> on 23 May.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969122–23Slattade_Grummond200376Lynch200672Arana2013140_184-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969122–23Slattade_Grummond200376Lynch200672Arana2013140-184">[182]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 2 January 1814, Bolívar was made the <a href="/wiki/Dictator" title="Dictator">dictator</a> of a <a href="/wiki/Second_Republic_of_Venezuela" title="Second Republic of Venezuela">Second Republic of Venezuela</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch200677_185-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch200677-185">[183]</a></sup> which retained the weaknesses of the first republic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014125_186-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014125-186">[184]</a></sup> Though all of Venezuela but <a href="/wiki/Maracaibo" title="Maracaibo">Maracaibo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coro,_Venezuela" title="Coro, Venezuela">Coro</a>, and Guayana was controlled by Republicans,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch200677–78_187-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch200677–78-187">[185]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014122_188-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014122-188">[186]</a></sup> Bolívar only governed western Venezuela. The east was controlled by <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Mari%C3%B1o" title="Santiago Mariño">Santiago Mariño</a>, a Venezuelan Republican who had fought Monteverde in the east throughout 1813.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969138–39Slattade_Grummond200375,_85Lynch200676–78_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969138–39Slattade_Grummond200375,_85Lynch200676–78-189">[187]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014118–19_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014118–19-190">[188]</a></sup> Mariño was unwilling to recognize Bolívar as his superior and Bolívar,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969140Langley200947Arana2013150_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969140Langley200947Arana2013150-191">[189]</a></sup> already rebuffing requests to restore the 1811 constitution,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELangley200947,_49Arana2013149–50_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELangley200947,_49Arana2013149–50-192">[190]</a></sup> desired a single, centralized, and stable Venezuelan republic under his governance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014121–22_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014121–22-193">[191]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969134,_140Lynch200678Arana2013149–50_194-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969134,_140Lynch200678Arana2013149–50-194">[192]</a></sup> Venezuela, however, was economically devastated and could not support the republic's armies,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969135Langley200949_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969135Langley200949-195">[193]</a></sup> and people of color remained disenfranchised and thus unsupportive of the republic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200386Langley200948–49Arana2013153_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200386Langley200948–49Arana2013153-196">[194]</a></sup> The republic was assailed from all sides by slave revolts and Royalist forces,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014123–24_197-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014123–24-197">[195]</a></sup> especially the Legion of Hell, an army of <i><a href="/wiki/Llanero" title="Llanero">llaneros</a></i> – the colored cowboys of the <a href="/wiki/Llanos" title="Llanos">Llanos</a>, to the south – led by the Spanish warlord <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Tom%C3%A1s_Boves" title="José Tomás Boves">José Tomás Boves</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200385–87,_97Lynch200681–82Arana2013151–52_198-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200385–87,_97Lynch200681–82Arana2013151–52-198">[196]</a></sup> Beginning in February 1814, Boves surged out of the llanos and overwhelmed the republic, occupying Caracas on 16 July and destroying Mariño's powerbase – and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Urica" title="Battle of Urica">dying in battle</a> – on 5 December.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003100–04,_106–12Langley200950Arana2013156–59,_163–64_199-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003100–04,_106–12Langley200950Arana2013156–59,_163–64-199">[197]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014126–29_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014126–29-200">[198]</a></sup>
</p><p>As Boves approached Caracas, Bolívar ordered the city stripped of its gold and silver,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969161Slattade_Grummond2003106Lynch200686Arana2013159_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969161Slattade_Grummond2003106Lynch200686Arana2013159-201">[199]</a></sup> which was moved through La Guaira to <a href="/wiki/Barcelona,_Venezuela" title="Barcelona, Venezuela">Barcelona, Venezuela</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003107_202-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003107-202">[200]</a></sup> and from there to <a href="/wiki/Cuman%C3%A1" title="Cumaná">Cumaná</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969162_203-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969162-203">[201]</a></sup> Bolívar then led 20,000 of its citizens east.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969161Slattade_Grummond2003106Lynch200686Arana2013159_201-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969161Slattade_Grummond2003106Lynch200686Arana2013159-201">[199]</a></sup> He arrived in Barcelona on 2 August,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003108Arana2013160_204-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003108Arana2013160-204">[202]</a></sup> but following <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Aragua_de_Barcelona&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Battle of Aragua de Barcelona (page does not exist)">another Royalist victory</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Batalla_de_Aragua_de_Barcelona" title="es:Batalla de Aragua de Barcelona">es</a>]</span> at <a href="/wiki/Aragua_de_Barcelona" title="Aragua de Barcelona">Aragua de Barcelona</a> on 17 August 1814, he moved to Cumaná.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969161–62Slattade_Grummond2003108Lynch200686–87Arana2013161_205-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969161–62Slattade_Grummond2003108Lynch200686–87Arana2013161-205">[203]</a></sup> On 26 August, he sailed with Mariño to <a href="/wiki/Margarita_Island" title="Margarita Island">Margarita Island</a> with the treasure. The officer in control of the island, <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Piar" title="Manuel Piar">Manuel Piar</a>, however, declared Bolívar and Mariño to be traitors, and forced them to return to the mainland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003108–09Lynch200687_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003108–09Lynch200687-206">[204]</a></sup> There, Ribas also accused Bolívar and Mariño of treachery, confiscated the treasure,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003109Lynch200687Arana2013162–63_207-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003109Lynch200687Arana2013162–63-207">[205]</a></sup> and then exiled the two on 8 September.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969163Arana2013163_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969163Arana2013163-208">[206]</a></sup> Bolívar arrived in Cartagena on 19 September and then met with the New Granadan congress in <a href="/wiki/Tunja" title="Tunja">Tunja</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969165–66Slattade_Grummond2003110–11Lynch200688_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969165–66Slattade_Grummond2003110–11Lynch200688-209">[207]</a></sup> which tasked him with subduing the rival <a href="/wiki/Free_and_Independent_State_of_Cundinamarca" title="Free and Independent State of Cundinamarca">Free and Independent State of Cundinamarca</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969167Lynch200689Langley200954_210-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969167Lynch200689Langley200954-210">[208]</a></sup> On 12 December, Bolívar captured Cundinamarca's capital, <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1" title="Bogotá">Bogotá</a>, and was given command of New Granada's armies in January 1815.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003111–13Lynch200688–89Arana2013168_211-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003111–13Lynch200688–89Arana2013168-211">[209]</a></sup> Bolívar next grappled with del Castillo, who had taken control of Cartagena.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969168–70Slattade_Grummond2003113–14Lynch200689–90Langley200955Arana2013169–70_212-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969168–70Slattade_Grummond2003113–14Lynch200689–90Langley200955Arana2013169–70-212">[210]</a></sup> Bolívar began <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Bol%C3%ADvar%27s_siege_of_Cartagena&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Bolívar's siege of Cartagena (page does not exist)">a six-week siege of the city</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asedio_neogranadino_de_Cartagena_de_Indias_(1815)" title="es:Asedio neogranadino de Cartagena de Indias (1815)">es</a>]</span> that allowed the Royalists to regain control of the Magdalena.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003114Lynch200689–90Arana2013169–70_213-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003114Lynch200689–90Arana2013169–70-213">[211]</a></sup> On 8 May, Bolívar made a truce with del Castillo, resigned his command, and sailed for exile on <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969170–71Slattade_Grummond2003114Langley200955Arana2013170–71_214-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969170–71Slattade_Grummond2003114Langley200955Arana2013170–71-214">[212]</a></sup> In July, 8,000 Spanish soldiers commanded by Spanish general <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Morillo" title="Pablo Morillo">Pablo Morillo</a> landed at <a href="/wiki/Santa_Marta" title="Santa Marta">Santa Marta</a> and then <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_siege_of_Cartagena&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Spanish siege of Cartagena (page does not exist)">besieged Cartagena</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asedio_espa%C3%B1ol_de_Cartagena_de_Indias_(1815)" title="es:Asedio español de Cartagena de Indias (1815)">es</a>]</span>, which capitulated on 6 December; del Castillo was executed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969173–74Slattade_Grummond2003115Lynch200690172–73Arana2013_215-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969173–74Slattade_Grummond2003115Lynch200690172–73Arana2013-215">[213]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014138_216-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014138-216">[214]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Jamaica.2C_Haiti.2C_Venezuela.2C_and_New_Granada.2C_1815.E2.80.931819"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Jamaica,_Haiti,_Venezuela,_and_New_Granada,_1815–1819">Jamaica, Haiti, Venezuela, and New Granada, 1815–1819</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Jamaica, Haiti, Venezuela, and New Granada, 1815–1819">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Portrait_of_Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar_by_Arturo_Michelena.jpg"><img alt="Portrait of Bolívar by Arturo Michelena" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6408" data-file-width="3216" decoding="async" height="339" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Portrait_of_Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar_by_Arturo_Michelena.jpg/170px-Portrait_of_Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar_by_Arturo_Michelena.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Portrait_of_Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar_by_Arturo_Michelena.jpg/255px-Portrait_of_Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar_by_Arturo_Michelena.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Portrait_of_Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar_by_Arturo_Michelena.jpg/340px-Portrait_of_Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar_by_Arturo_Michelena.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Portrait_of_Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar_by_Arturo_Michelena.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1895 portrait of Bolívar by Arturo Michelena</div></div></div>
<p>Bolívar arrived in <a href="/wiki/Kingston,_Jamaica" title="Kingston, Jamaica">Kingston, Jamaica</a>, on 14 May 1815 and,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003116Lynch200690_217-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003116Lynch200690-217">[215]</a></sup> like his earlier exile on Curaçao, ruminated on the fall of the Venezuelan and New Granadan republics. He wrote extensively, requesting assistance from Britain and corresponding with merchants based in the Caribbean. This culminated in September 1815 with the <a href="/wiki/Letter_from_Jamaica" title="Letter from Jamaica">Letter from Jamaica</a>, in which Bolívar again laid out his ideology and vision of the future of the Americas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969184–85,_190Slattade_Grummond2003124–27Lynch200692,_95Langley200955–57Arana2013174–76_218-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969184–85,_190Slattade_Grummond2003124–27Lynch200692,_95Langley200955–57Arana2013174–76-218">[216]</a></sup> On 9 December, the Venezuelan pirate <a href="/wiki/Renato_Beluche" title="Renato Beluche">Renato Beluche</a> brought Bolívar news from New Granada and asked him to join the Republican community in exile in <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003128–29_219-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003128–29-219">[217]</a></sup> Bolívar tentatively accepted and that night escaped assassination by his manservant, who mistakenly killed Bolívar's <a href="/wiki/Paymaster" title="Paymaster">paymaster</a> as part of a Spanish plot.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969183Slattade_Grummond2003129Lynch200696–97Arana2013177_220-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969183Slattade_Grummond2003129Lynch200696–97Arana2013177-220">[218]</a></sup> He left Jamaica eight days later,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969191Lynch200697Arana2013177–78_221-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969191Lynch200697Arana2013177–78-221">[219]</a></sup> arrived in <a href="/wiki/Les_Cayes" title="Les Cayes">Les Cayes</a> on 24 December,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003129Langley200959Arana2013178_222-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003129Langley200959Arana2013178-222">[220]</a></sup> and on 2 January 1816 was introduced to <a href="/wiki/Alexandre_P%C3%A9tion" title="Alexandre Pétion">Alexandre Pétion</a>, President of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Haiti_(1806%E2%80%931820)" title="Republic of Haiti (1806–1820)">Republic of Haiti</a> by a mutual friend.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969192Slattade_Grummond2003130Lynch200697Langley200959Arana2013178–79_223-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969192Slattade_Grummond2003130Lynch200697Langley200959Arana2013178–79-223">[221]</a></sup> Bolívar and Pétion impressed and befriended each other and,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969192–93Slattade_Grummond2003130Arana2013179_224-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969192–93Slattade_Grummond2003130Arana2013179-224">[222]</a></sup> after Bolívar pledged to free every slave in the areas he occupied, Pétion gave him money and military supplies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969193Slattade_Grummond2003130Lynch200697Arana2013179_225-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969193Slattade_Grummond2003130Lynch200697Arana2013179-225">[223]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014313_226-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014313-226">[224]</a></sup>
</p><p>Returning to Les Cayes, Bolívar held a conference with the Republican leaders in Haiti and was made supreme leader with Mariño as his chief of staff.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969194–95Slattade_Grummond2003131–32Arana2013179_227-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969194–95Slattade_Grummond2003131–32Arana2013179-227">[225]</a></sup> The Republicans departed Les Cayes for Venezuela on 31 March 1816 and followed the <a href="/wiki/Antilles" title="Antilles">Antilles</a> eastward.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969195Lynch2006100Arana2013183_228-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969195Lynch2006100Arana2013183-228">[226]</a></sup> After a delay to allow a lover of Bolívar's to join the fleet, it arrived on 2 May at Margarita Island, controlled by Republican commander <a href="/wiki/Juan_Bautista_Arismendi" title="Juan Bautista Arismendi">Juan Bautista Arismendi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003137–38Lynch2006100Arana2013183–84_229-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003137–38Lynch2006100Arana2013183–84-229">[227]</a></sup> Bolívar next moved to the mainland, where he declared the emancipation of all slaves and annulled of the Decree of War to the Death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969197–98Slattade_Grummond2003141–42Lynch2006100Langley200960Arana2013186_230-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969197–98Slattade_Grummond2003141–42Lynch2006100Langley200960Arana2013186-230">[228]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[c]</a></sup> He took <a href="/wiki/Car%C3%BApano" title="Carúpano">Carúpano</a> on 31 May and sent Mariño and Piar into Guayana to build their own army,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969197Slattade_Grummond2003139–40_234-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969197Slattade_Grummond2003139–40-234">[231]</a></sup> and then <a href="/wiki/Ocumare_de_la_Costa" title="Ocumare de la Costa">Ocumare de la Costa</a> on 6 July.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969199Slattade_Grummond2003141–42Lynch2006100_235-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969199Slattade_Grummond2003141–42Lynch2006100-235">[232]</a></sup> There, by 14 July, his forces were defeated and scattered by a Royalist force that then captured Ocumare and the Haitian supplies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969198–200Slattade_Grummond2003142–44_236-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969198–200Slattade_Grummond2003142–44-236">[233]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014314_237-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014314-237">[234]</a></sup> Bolívar fled by sea to <a href="/wiki/G%C3%BCiria" title="Güiria">Güiria</a> where, on 22 August, he was deposed by Mariño and <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Francisco_Berm%C3%BAdez" title="José Francisco Bermúdez">José Francisco Bermúdez</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969202Lynch2006101Arana2013189_238-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969202Lynch2006101Arana2013189-238">[235]</a></sup> who tried to kill Bolívar with a sword.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969202Arana2013189_239-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969202Arana2013189-239">[236]</a></sup>
</p><p>Bolívar returned to Haiti by early September,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003147–48Arana2013190_240-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003147–48Arana2013190-240">[237]</a></sup> where Pétion again agreed to assist him again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969203Slattade_Grummond2003146Lynch2006101Arana2013189_241-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969203Slattade_Grummond2003146Lynch2006101Arana2013189-241">[238]</a></sup> In his absence, the Republican leaders scattered across Venezuela, concentrating in the Llanos, and became disunited warlords.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003146Arana2013190–91_242-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003146Arana2013190–91-242">[239]</a></sup> These <i><a href="/wiki/Caudillo" title="Caudillo">caudillos</a></i> declined to recognize Mariño's leadership,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969203Arana2013191_243-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969203Arana2013191-243">[240]</a></sup> and instead sought Bolívar's return. Arismendi wrote to Bolívar and dispatched New Granadan Republican <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Antonio_Zea" title="Francisco Antonio Zea">Francisco Antonio Zea</a> to convince him to return. Bolívar and Zea set sail for Venezuela on 21 December with <a href="/wiki/Luis_Bri%C3%B3n" title="Luis Brión">Luis Brión</a>, a Dutch merchant,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969203Slattade_Grummond2003150–51Arana2013190–91_244-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969203Slattade_Grummond2003150–51Arana2013190–91-244">[241]</a></sup> and arrived ten days later at Barcelona. There, Bolívar issued a decree announcing his return and calling for a congress for a new, <a href="/wiki/Third_Republic_of_Venezuela" title="Third Republic of Venezuela">third republic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003151–52Lynch2006102_245-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003151–52Lynch2006102-245">[242]</a></sup> He wrote to the Republican <i>caudillos</i>, especially <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Antonio_P%C3%A1ez" title="José Antonio Páez">José Antonio Páez</a>, who controlled most of the western Llanos, to unite under his leadership.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003146–47Lynch2006102Arana2013191–92_246-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003146–47Lynch2006102Arana2013191–92-246">[243]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014313–15_247-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014313–15-247">[244]</a></sup> On 8 January 1817, Bolívar marched towards Caracas but <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Clarines&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Battle of Clarines (page does not exist)">was turned back</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Batalla_de_Clarines" title="es:Batalla de Clarines">es</a>]</span> and then pursued to Barcelona by a larger Royalist force.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003152Arana2013192_248-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003152Arana2013192-248">[245]</a></sup> At Bolívar's request, Mariño arrived on 8 February with Bermúdez, who then reconciled with Bolívar, and forced a Royalist withdrawal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969208–09Arana2013192–93_249-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969208–09Arana2013192–93-249">[246]</a></sup>
</p><p>Even with their combined forces, however, Bolívar, Mariño, and Bermúdez could not hold Barcelona.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003153Lynch2006102Arana2013193_250-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003153Lynch2006102Arana2013193-250">[247]</a></sup> Instead, on 25 March 1817,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969210Arana2013195_251-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969210Arana2013195-251">[248]</a></sup> Bolívar began moving south to join Piar in Guayana, Piar's power base, and establish his own economic and political base there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969207–08Slattade_Grummond2003153Lynch2006102–03Arana2013193_252-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969207–08Slattade_Grummond2003153Lynch2006102–03Arana2013193-252">[249]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014315_253-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014315-253">[250]</a></sup> Bolívar met Piar on 4 April,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969210Slattade_Grummond2003154_254-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969210Slattade_Grummond2003154-254">[251]</a></sup> promoted him to the rank of <a href="/wiki/General_of_the_army" title="General of the army">general of the army</a>, and then joined a force of Piar's troops besieging the city of Angostura (now <a href="/wiki/Ciudad_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Ciudad Bolívar">Ciudad Bolívar</a>) on 2 May.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969211Slattade_Grummond2003155Lynch2006103–04Arana2013195–96_255-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969211Slattade_Grummond2003155Lynch2006103–04Arana2013195–96-255">[252]</a></sup> Meanwhile, Mariño went east to reestablish his power base and on 8 May convened a congress of ten men, including Brión and Zea, that named Mariño as supreme commander of the Republican forces and reinstated the 1811 constitution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969211,_213Slattade_Grummond2003153–54,_156Arana2013200–02_256-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969211,_213Slattade_Grummond2003153–54,_156Arana2013200–02-256">[253]</a></sup> This backfired and provoked the defection of 30 officers, including <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Urdaneta" title="Rafael Urdaneta">Rafael Urdaneta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Jos%C3%A9_de_Sucre" title="Antonio José de Sucre">Antonio José de Sucre</a>, to Bolívar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969213–14Slattade_Grummond2003156Lynch2006104Arana2013202_257-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969213–14Slattade_Grummond2003156Lynch2006104Arana2013202-257">[254]</a></sup> On 30 June, Bolívar granted Piar <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leave_of_absence" title="Leave of absence">leave of absence</a> at his request,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969217Lynch2006106Arana2013197_258-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969217Lynch2006106Arana2013197-258">[255]</a></sup> and then issued an arrest warrant for Piar on 23 July after he began fomenting rebellion, alleging that Bolívar had dismissed him because of his African heritage. Piar was captured on 27 September as he fled to join Mariño was brought to Angostura, where he was executed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Firing_squad" title="Firing squad">firing squad</a> on 16 October.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969217–18Slattade_Grummond2003158–60Arana2013197–99_259-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969217–18Slattade_Grummond2003158–60Arana2013197–99-259">[256]</a></sup> Bolívar then sent Sucre to reconcile with Mariño,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969220Slattade_Grummond2003160Arana2013202–03_260-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969220Slattade_Grummond2003160Arana2013202–03-260">[257]</a></sup> who pledged loyalty to Bolívar on 26 January 1818.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003160_261-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003160-261">[258]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 17 July 1817, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Second_Battle_of_Angostura&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Second Battle of Angostura (page does not exist)">Angostura fell</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Segunda_Batalla_de_Angostura" title="es:Segunda Batalla de Angostura">es</a>]</span> to Bolívar's forces, which then gained control of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orinoco_River" title="Orinoco River">Orinoco River</a> in early August.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969215Slattade_Grummond2003157Arana2013201_262-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969215Slattade_Grummond2003157Arana2013201-262">[259]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014317–18_263-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014317–18-263">[260]</a></sup> Angostura became the provisional Republican capital and in September,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003163_264-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003163-264">[261]</a></sup> Bolívar began creating formal political and military structures for the republic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003163Lynch2006110–12_265-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003163Lynch2006110–12-265">[262]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014319_266-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014319-266">[263]</a></sup> Bolívar then gained recognition as supreme leader from Páez, whom he met at <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_de_Payara" title="San Juan de Payara">San Juan de Payara</a> on 30 January 1818.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch2006113–14Arana2013207_267-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch2006113–14Arana2013207-267">[264]</a></sup> In February 1818, the Republicans moved north and took <a href="/wiki/Calabozo" title="Calabozo">Calabozo</a>, where <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Calabozo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Battle of Calabozo (page does not exist)">they defeated Morillo</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Batalla_de_Calabozo" title="es:Batalla de Calabozo">es</a>]</span>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969231–32Slattade_Grummond2003171–72Lynch2006115Arana2013209–11_268-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969231–32Slattade_Grummond2003171–72Lynch2006115Arana2013209–11-268">[265]</a></sup> who had returned to Venezuela a year earlier after <a href="/wiki/Spanish_reconquest_of_New_Granada" title="Spanish reconquest of New Granada">conquering Republican New Granada</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014317_269-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014317-269">[266]</a></sup> Bolívar next advanced towards Caracas and on 16 March was <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Third_Battle_of_La_Puerta&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Third Battle of La Puerta (page does not exist)">himself defeated</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Batalla_de_La_Puerta_(1818)" title="es:Batalla de La Puerta (1818)">es</a>]</span>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969234–35Slattade_Grummond2003173Lynch2006116Arana2013211–12_270-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969234–35Slattade_Grummond2003173Lynch2006116Arana2013211–12-270">[267]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014321–22_271-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014321–22-271">[268]</a></sup> and was almost assassinated by Spanish infiltrators in April. Illness and additional Republican defeats obliged Bolívar to return to Angostura in May. For the rest of the year, he focused on administrating the republic, rebuilding its armed forces,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969235–37,_243Slattade_Grummond2003174–80Lynch2006116–17Arana2013212–17_272-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969235–37,_243Slattade_Grummond2003174–80Lynch2006116–17Arana2013212–17-272">[269]</a></sup> and organizing elections for a national congress that would meet in 1819.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969244Lynch2006117_273-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969244Lynch2006117-273">[270]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014325_274-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014325-274">[271]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Gran_Colombia.2C_1819.E2.80.931830"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Gran_Colombia,_1819–1830">Gran Colombia, 1819–1830</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Gran Colombia, 1819–1830">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Equestrian_portrait_of_Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar.jpg"><img alt="Equestrian portrait of Bolívar" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1540" data-file-width="1104" decoding="async" height="307" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Equestrian_portrait_of_Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar.jpg/220px-Equestrian_portrait_of_Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Equestrian_portrait_of_Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar.jpg/330px-Equestrian_portrait_of_Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Equestrian_portrait_of_Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar.jpg/440px-Equestrian_portrait_of_Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Equestrian_portrait_of_Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1826</span> equestrian portrait of Bolívar by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Hilari%C3%B3n_Ibarra&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="José Hilarión Ibarra (page does not exist)">José Hilarión Ibarra</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Hilari%C3%B3n_Ibarra" title="es:José Hilarión Ibarra">es</a>]</span></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Angostura" title="Congress of Angostura">congress met in Angostura</a> on 15 February 1819.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969245Slattade_Grummond2003180Lynch2006119Arana2013222_275-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969245Slattade_Grummond2003180Lynch2006119Arana2013222-275">[272]</a></sup> There, Bolívar gave a speech in which he presented his draft of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Venezuelan_Constitution_of_1819&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Venezuelan Constitution of 1819 (page does not exist)">a constitution</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constituci%C3%B3n_de_Venezuela_de_1819" title="es:Constitución de Venezuela de 1819">es</a>]</span> for a centralized government modeled on the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Government of the United Kingdom">British government</a>, advocated for racial equality,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969246–53Lynch2006120–22Arana2013222–25_276-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969246–53Lynch2006120–22Arana2013222–25-276">[273]</a></sup> and relinquished civil authority to the congress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969246Arana2013222_277-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969246Arana2013222-277">[274]</a></sup> On 16 February, the congress elected Bolívar as president and Zea as vice president.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014325_274-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014325-274">[271]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969254Slattade_Grummond2003180Arana2013225_278-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969254Slattade_Grummond2003180Arana2013225-278">[275]</a></sup> On 27 February,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969255_279-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969255-279">[276]</a></sup> Bolívar left Angostura to rejoin Páez in the west and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Apure_campaign&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Apure campaign (page does not exist)">resumed campaigning</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Campa%C3%B1a_de_Apure" title="es:Campaña de Apure">es</a>]</span>, indecisively, against Morillo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014325_274-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014325-274">[271]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969255–58Slattade_Grummond2003180–81Lynch2006126Arana2013226–28_280-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969255–58Slattade_Grummond2003180–81Lynch2006126Arana2013226–28-280">[277]</a></sup> In May, as the annual <a href="/wiki/Wet_season" title="Wet season">wet season</a> was beginning in the Llanos, Bolívar met with his officers and revealed his intention to invade New Granada,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969263Slattade_Grummond2003183Lynch2006127Arana2013228–29_281-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969263Slattade_Grummond2003183Lynch2006127Arana2013228–29-281">[278]</a></sup> which he had prepared for by sending Santander to build up Republican forces in <a href="/wiki/Casanare_Province" title="Casanare Province">Casanare Province</a> in August 1818.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003176Lynch2006124_282-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003176Lynch2006124-282">[279]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014324–25_283-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014324–25-283">[280]</a></sup> On 27 May,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003183Lynch2006127_284-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003183Lynch2006127-284">[281]</a></sup> Bolívar marched with more than 2,000 soldiers toward the <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andes</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch2006127Langley200975Arana2013228_285-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch2006127Langley200975Arana2013228-285">[282]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014326–27_286-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014326–27-286">[283]</a></sup> and left Páez, Mariño, Urdaneta, and Bermúdez to tie down Morillo's forces in Venezuela.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch2006127Arana2013229–30_287-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch2006127Arana2013229–30-287">[284]</a></sup>
</p><p>Bolívar entered Casanare Province with his army on 4 June 1819,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003184Arana2013230_288-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003184Arana2013230-288">[285]</a></sup> then met up with Santander at <a href="/wiki/Tame,_Arauca" title="Tame, Arauca">Tame, Arauca</a>, on 11 June.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969264Slattade_Grummond2003184Lynch2006128Arana2013230–31_289-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969264Slattade_Grummond2003184Lynch2006128Arana2013230–31-289">[286]</a></sup> The combined Republican force reached the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Oriental_(Colombia)" title="Cordillera Oriental (Colombia)">Eastern Range</a> of the Andes on 22 June and began a grueling crossing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969166Slattade_Grummond2003185_290-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969166Slattade_Grummond2003185-290">[287]</a></sup> On 6 July, the Republicans descended the Andes from the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=P%C3%A1ramo_de_Pisba&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Páramo de Pisba (page does not exist)">Páramo de Pisba</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parque_nacional_natural_Pisba" title="es:Parque nacional natural Pisba">es</a>]</span> at <a href="/wiki/Socha" title="Socha">Socha</a> and into the plains of New Granada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch2006128Arana2013232_291-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch2006128Arana2013232-291">[288]</a></sup> After a brief convalescence, the Republicans <a href="/wiki/Bol%C3%ADvar%27s_campaign_to_liberate_New_Granada" title="Bolívar's campaign to liberate New Granada">made rapid progress</a> against the forces of Spanish colonel <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Barreiro_Manj%C3%B3n&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="José María Barreiro Manjón (page does not exist)">José María Barreiro Manjón</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Barreiro_Manj%C3%B3n" title="es:José María Barreiro Manjón">es</a>]</span> until, on 7 August, the Royalists were routed at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Boyac%C3%A1" title="Battle of Boyacá">Battle of Boyacá</a>. On 10 August, Bolívar entered Bogotá, which the Spanish officials had hastily abandoned,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969268–73Slattade_Grummond2003188–93Lynch2006128–30Langley200975Arana2013232–35_292-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969268–73Slattade_Grummond2003188–93Lynch2006128–30Langley200975Arana2013232–35-292">[289]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014327–28_293-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014327–28-293">[290]</a></sup> and captured the viceregal treasury and armories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003193Lynch2006130Arana2013235,_237_294-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003193Lynch2006130Arana2013235,_237-294">[291]</a></sup> After sending forces to secure Republican control of central New Granada,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969276Slattade_Grummond2003193,_195Lynch2006130–31_295-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969276Slattade_Grummond2003193,_195Lynch2006130–31-295">[292]</a></sup> Bolívar paraded through Bogotá on 18 September with Santander.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969280Lynch2006130Arana2013238–39_296-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969280Lynch2006130Arana2013238–39-296">[293]</a></sup>
</p><p>Desiring to merge New Granada and Venezuela into a "<a href="/wiki/Gran_Colombia" title="Gran Colombia">greater republic of Colombia</a>", Bolívar first established a provisional government in Bogotá with Santander,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969277,_280Lynch2006131Arana2013240–41_297-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969277,_280Lynch2006131Arana2013240–41-297">[294]</a></sup> and then left to resume campaigning against the Royalists in Venezuela on 20 September 1819.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003195Lynch2006131–32_298-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003195Lynch2006131–32-298">[295]</a></sup> En route, he learned that Santander had executed Barreiro and other Royalist prisoners on 11 October<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch2006132Arana2013241–42_299-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch2006132Arana2013241–42-299">[296]</a></sup> and that Zea had been replaced as vice president in September 1819 by Arismendi, who was conspiring with Mariño against Urdaneta and Bermúdez. Bolívar arrived in Angostura on 11 December and, by being conciliatory, restored order.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969282–83Slattade_Grummond2003196–97Lynch2006132–33Arana2013245–46_300-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969282–83Slattade_Grummond2003196–97Lynch2006132–33Arana2013245–46-300">[297]</a></sup> He then proposed the merging of New Granada and Venezuela to the congress on 14 December,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969283Slattade_Grummond2003197–98Arana2013246_301-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969283Slattade_Grummond2003197–98Arana2013246-301">[298]</a></sup> which was approved. On 17 December, the congress issued a decree creating the Republic of <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>, including the regions of Venezuela, New Granada, and the still Spanish-controlled <a href="/wiki/Real_Audiencia_of_Quito" title="Real Audiencia of Quito"><i>Real Audiencia</i> of Quito</a>, and elected Bolívar and Zea president and vice president respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969284Slattade_Grummond2003198Lynch2006134Arana2013246–47_302-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969284Slattade_Grummond2003198Lynch2006134Arana2013246–47-302">[299]</a></sup>
</p><p>After <a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">Christmas</a> Day, 1819,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969290Arana2013247_303-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969290Arana2013247-303">[300]</a></sup> Bolívar left Angostura to direct campaigns against Royalist forces along the Caribbean coasts of Venezuela and New Granada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969290Slattade_Grummond2003200–01Arana2013247_304-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969290Slattade_Grummond2003200–01Arana2013247-304">[301]</a></sup> He met with Santander in Bogotá in March 1820, then rode to Cúcuta and inspected Republican forces in northern Colombia over April and May 1820.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003201–02Lynch2006134,_136_305-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003201–02Lynch2006134,_136-305">[302]</a></sup> Meanwhile, Morillo's military and political position was fatally undermined by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=C%C3%A1diz_mutiny_of_1820&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Cádiz mutiny of 1820 (page does not exist)">mutiny of Spanish soldiers in Cádiz on 1 January</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pronunciamiento_de_Riego" title="es:Pronunciamiento de Riego">es</a>]</span>, which forced Ferdinand VII to accept <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Constitution_of_1812" title="Spanish Constitution of 1812">a liberal constitution</a> in March.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969291–92Slattade_Grummond2003204Lynch2006136Arana2013247–48_306-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969291–92Slattade_Grummond2003204Lynch2006136Arana2013247–48-306">[303]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014368_307-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014368-307">[304]</a></sup> News of the mutiny and its consequences arrived in Colombia in the same month and was followed by orders from Spain to Morillo to publicize the constitution and negotiate a peace that would return Colombia to the Spanish Empire. Bolívar and Morillo, seeking to gain leverage over each other,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969292–97Slattade_Grummond2003204–09Lynch2006136–37Arana2013248,_253–54_308-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969292–97Slattade_Grummond2003204–09Lynch2006136–37Arana2013248,_253–54-308">[305]</a></sup> delayed talks until 21 November, when Colombian and Royalist delegates met in <a href="/wiki/Trujillo,_Trujillo" title="Trujillo, Trujillo">Trujillo, Venezuela</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969297Slattade_Grummond2003209Arana2013254_309-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969297Slattade_Grummond2003209Arana2013254-309">[306]</a></sup> The delegates completed <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Trujillo_Armistice&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Trujillo Armistice (page does not exist)">two treaties</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tratado_de_Armisticio_y_Regularizaci%C3%B3n_de_la_Guerra" title="es:Tratado de Armisticio y Regularización de la Guerra">es</a>]</span> on 25 November, establishing a six-month truce, a <a href="/wiki/Prisoner_exchange" title="Prisoner exchange">prisoner exchange</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Law_of_war" title="Law of war">basic rights for combatants</a>. Bolívar and Morillo signed the treaties on 25 and 26 November, then met the next day at <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Santa_Ana_de_Trujillo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Santa Ana de Trujillo (page does not exist)">Santa Ana de Trujillo</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Santa_Ana_de_Trujillo" title="es:Santa Ana de Trujillo">es</a>]</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969297Slattade_Grummond2003209–10Lynch2006137Arana2013254–55_310-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969297Slattade_Grummond2003209–10Lynch2006137Arana2013254–55-310">[307]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014388–89_311-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014388–89-311">[308]</a></sup> After this meeting, Morillo turned his command over to Spanish general <a href="/wiki/Miguel_de_la_Torre" title="Miguel de la Torre">Miguel de la Torre</a> and departed for Spain on 17 December.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003211Lynch2006138Arana2013257_312-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003211Lynch2006138Arana2013257-312">[309]</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 1821, as Bolívar was traveling from Bogotá to Cúcuta in anticipation of the opening of <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_C%C3%BAcuta" title="Congress of Cúcuta">a new congress there</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969303Slattade_Grummond2003216_313-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969303Slattade_Grummond2003216-313">[310]</a></sup> he learned that Royalist-controlled Maracaibo had defected to Colombia and been occupied by Urdaneta.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969302–03Slattade_Grummond2003216Lynch2006139_314-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969302–03Slattade_Grummond2003216Lynch2006139-314">[311]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014391_315-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014391-315">[312]</a></sup> La Torre protested to Bolívar, who refused to return Maracaibo, leading to a renewal of hostilities on 28 April.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969304Slattade_Grummond2003218Arana2013263_316-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969304Slattade_Grummond2003218Arana2013263-316">[313]</a></sup> Over May and June, Colombia's armies made rapid progress until, on 24 June, Bolívar and Páez decisively defeated La Torre at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Carabobo" title="Battle of Carabobo">Battle of Carabobo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969304–07Slattade_Grummond2003218–20Lynch2006139–40Arana2013263–65_317-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969304–07Slattade_Grummond2003218–20Lynch2006139–40Arana2013263–65-317">[314]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014391–92_318-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014391–92-318">[315]</a></sup> All Royalist forces remaining in Venezuela were eliminated by August 1823.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014392_319-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014392-319">[316]</a></sup> Bolívar entered Caracas in triumph on 29 June,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003221Arana2013267_320-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003221Arana2013267-320">[317]</a></sup> and issued a decree on 16 July dividing Venezuela into three military zones governed by Páez, Bermúdez, and Mariño.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch2006141–42Arana2013266_321-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch2006141–42Arana2013266-321">[318]</a></sup> Bolívar then met with the Congress of Cúcuta,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003221Arana2013271_322-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003221Arana2013271-322">[319]</a></sup> which had ratified the formation of Gran Colombia and elected him as president and Santander as vice president in September. Bolívar accepted and was sworn in on 3 October, although he protested the establishment of a precedent of military leaders as head of the Colombian state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969308–10Slattade_Grummond2003221Lynch2006145–46Arana2013271_323-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969308–10Slattade_Grummond2003221Lynch2006145–46Arana2013271-323">[320]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="Ecuador.2C_Peru.2C_and_Bolivia.2C_1821.E2.80.931825"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecuador,_Peru,_and_Bolivia,_1821–1825">Ecuador, Peru, and Bolivia, 1821–1825</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Ecuador, Peru, and Bolivia, 1821–1825">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Josedesanmartin.jpg"><img alt="Engraving of José de San Martín" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="555" data-file-width="459" decoding="async" height="206" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Josedesanmartin.jpg/170px-Josedesanmartin.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Josedesanmartin.jpg/255px-Josedesanmartin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Josedesanmartin.jpg/340px-Josedesanmartin.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Josedesanmartin.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1901 engraving of <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_San_Mart%C3%ADn" title="José de San Martín">José de San Martín</a></div></div></div>
<p>After the Battle of Carabobo, Bolívar turned his attention south, to <a href="/wiki/Pasto,_Colombia" title="Pasto, Colombia">Pasto, Colombia</a>; Quito and the <a href="/wiki/Free_Province_of_Guayaquil" title="Free Province of Guayaquil">Free Province of Guayaquil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a>; and the <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_Peru" title="Viceroyalty of Peru">Viceroyalty of Peru</a>. Pasto and Quito were Royalist strongholds,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014392_319-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014392-319">[316]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969313–14Slattade_Grummond2003224Lynch2006167_324-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969313–14Slattade_Grummond2003224Lynch2006167-324">[321]</a></sup> while Guayaquil had declared its independence on 9 October 1820<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch2006167_325-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch2006167-325">[322]</a></sup> and had been garrisoned by Sucre on Bolívar's orders in January 1821.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969302,_319Lynch2006138–39,_168_326-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969302,_319Lynch2006138–39,_168-326">[323]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a> declared its independence on 28 November 1821 and joined Colombia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969317Slattade_Grummond2003222Lynch2006167_327-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969317Slattade_Grummond2003222Lynch2006167-327">[324]</a></sup> Peru had been invaded by <a href="/wiki/Liberating_Expedition_of_Peru" title="Liberating Expedition of Peru">a Republican army</a> led by Argentine general <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_San_Mart%C3%ADn" title="José de San Martín">José de San Martín</a>, who had <a href="/wiki/Chilean_War_of_Independence" title="Chilean War of Independence">liberated Chile</a> and Peru,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003213–15Langley200979Arana2013271–77_328-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003213–15Langley200979Arana2013271–77-328">[325]</a></sup> and Bolívar feared San Martín would absorb Ecuador into Peru.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969317Slattade_Grummond2003224–25Lynch2006167Arana2013278_329-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969317Slattade_Grummond2003224–25Lynch2006167Arana2013278-329">[326]</a></sup> In October 1821, after congress empowered him to secure Ecuador for Colombia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969312Lynch2006146_330-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969312Lynch2006146-330">[327]</a></sup> Bolívar assembled an army in Bogotá that departed on 13 December 1821.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969321Slattade_Grummond2003221Lynch2006146,_168Arana2013278–79_331-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969321Slattade_Grummond2003221Lynch2006146,_168Arana2013278–79-331">[328]</a></sup> His advance was halted by illness and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Bombon%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Battle of Bomboná (page does not exist)">a Pyrrhic victory</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Batalla_de_Bombon%C3%A1" title="es:Batalla de Bomboná">es</a>]</span> in southern Colombia on 7 April 1822.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014393_332-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014393-332">[329]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969323–25Slattade_Grummond2003226Lynch2006169Arana2013281–83_333-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969323–25Slattade_Grummond2003226Lynch2006169Arana2013281–83-333">[330]</a></sup>
</p><p>To the south, Sucre, who had been trapped in Guayaquil by Royalist advances from Quito,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969320Lynch2006168Arana2013280_334-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969320Lynch2006168Arana2013280-334">[331]</a></sup> now advanced, decisively defeated the Royalists at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Pichincha" title="Battle of Pichincha">Battle of Pichincha</a> on 24 May 1822, and occupied Quito.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014393_332-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014393-332">[329]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969325Slattade_Grummond2003226–27Lynch2006170Langley200980–81Arana201328–88_335-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969325Slattade_Grummond2003226–27Lynch2006170Langley200980–81Arana201328–88-335">[332]</a></sup> On 6 June, Pasto surrendered,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969325–26Slattade_Grummond2003227_336-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969325–26Slattade_Grummond2003227-336">[333]</a></sup> and ten days later Bolívar paraded through Quito with Sucre.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969327Lynch2006170–71Arana2013287–88_337-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969327Lynch2006170–71Arana2013287–88-337">[334]</a></sup> He also met the Ecuadorian Republican <a href="/wiki/Manuela_S%C3%A1enz" title="Manuela Sáenz">Manuela Sáenz</a>, the wife of a British merchant, with whom he began a lasting affair.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969327Slattade_Grummond2003228,_230Lynch2006171,_178–79Langley200981Arana2013289–90_338-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969327Slattade_Grummond2003228,_230Lynch2006171,_178–79Langley200981Arana2013289–90-338">[335]</a></sup> From Quito, Bolívar traveled to Guayaquil in anticipation of a meeting with San Martín to discuss the city's status and rallied support for its annexation by Colombia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969328,_330–31Slattade_Grummond2003234Lynch2006171–72Arana2013292_339-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969328,_330–31Slattade_Grummond2003234Lynch2006171–72Arana2013292-339">[336]</a></sup> By the time San Martín arrived in Guayaquil on 26 July,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969331Slattade_Grummond2003235Arana2013295–96_340-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969331Slattade_Grummond2003235Arana2013295–96-340">[337]</a></sup> Bolívar had already secured Guayaquil for Colombia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969331Slattade_Grummond2003235Lynch2006172Langley200981–82_341-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969331Slattade_Grummond2003235Lynch2006172Langley200981–82-341">[338]</a></sup> and the two-day <a href="/wiki/Guayaquil_Conference" title="Guayaquil Conference">Guayaquil Conference</a> produced little. Ill, politically isolated, and disillusioned, San Martín subsequently resigned from his offices and went into exile.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969331,_338–41Slattade_Grummond2003235–37Lynch2006173–75Langley200982Arana2013295–305_342-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969331,_338–41Slattade_Grummond2003235–37Lynch2006173–75Langley200982Arana2013295–305-342">[339]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014394–95_343-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014394–95-343">[340]</a></sup>
</p><p>Over the rest of 1822, Bolívar traveled around Ecuador to complete its annexation while dispatching officers to suppress repeated rebellions in Pasto and resisting calls to return to Bogotá or Venezuela.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969343–45Slattade_Grummond2003240–41Lynch2006175–76Arana2013306–07_344-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969343–45Slattade_Grummond2003240–41Lynch2006175–76Arana2013306–07-344">[341]</a></sup> Meanwhile, Royalist forces under general <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_Canterac" title="José de Canterac">José de Canterac</a> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Second_Intermediate_campaign&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Second Intermediate campaign (page does not exist)">overwhelmed the Peruvian republic</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Segunda_Campa%C3%B1a_de_Intermedios" title="es:Segunda Campaña de Intermedios">es</a>]</span> and briefly took <a href="/wiki/Lima" title="Lima">Lima</a>, Peru's capital, in June 1823.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003243Arana2013305,_308_345-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003243Arana2013305,_308-345">[342]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014395–96_346-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014395–96-346">[343]</a></sup> After initially refusing Colombian assistance,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969353Slattade_Grummond2003241Lynch2006183_347-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969353Slattade_Grummond2003241Lynch2006183-347">[344]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_the_Republic_of_Peru" title="Congress of the Republic of Peru">Peruvian congress</a> asked Bolívar several times in 1823 to assume command of their forces. Bolívar responded by sending an army under Sucre to assist, and requested permission from the Colombian congress to lead troops into Peru himself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969354–56Slattade_Grummond2003242–43Arana2013308–09_348-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969354–56Slattade_Grummond2003242–43Arana2013308–09-348">[345]</a></sup> On 3 August, Bolívar received that permission and set sail for Lima,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969356Lynch2006184_349-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969356Lynch2006184-349">[346]</a></sup> where he arrived to much fanfare on 1 September.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003243–44Lynch2006185Langley200986Arana2013310–11_350-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003243–44Lynch2006185Langley200986Arana2013310–11-350">[347]</a></sup> When Bolívar arrived, Peru was split between four Republican armies and two rival presidents, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_la_Riva_Ag%C3%BCero" title="José de la Riva Agüero">José de la Riva Agüero</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Bernardo_de_Tagle_y_Portocarrero,_Marquis_of_Torre_Tagle" title="José Bernardo de Tagle y Portocarrero, Marquis of Torre Tagle">José Bernardo de Tagle</a>; the Royalists, based out of the region of <a href="/wiki/Upper_Peru" title="Upper Peru">Upper Peru</a>; and Bolívar, whom the Peruvian congress invested with supreme military authority.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003243–44Lynch2006185Langley200986–87Arana2013312_351-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003243–44Lynch2006185Langley200986–87Arana2013312-351">[348]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014398_352-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014398-352">[349]</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 1823, a faction of officers serving Riva Agüero, who plotted with the Royalists against Bolívar, mutinied and handed him to Bolívar, who exiled Riva Agüero from Peru.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969362Slattade_Grummond2003244Lynch2006185–86_353-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969362Slattade_Grummond2003244Lynch2006185–86-353">[350]</a></sup> Bolívar next struggled to build an army in Peru with few resources, and without support from Colombia or its allies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014398_352-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014398-352">[349]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969362–63Arana2013314_354-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969362–63Arana2013314-354">[351]</a></sup> On 1 January 1824, Bolívar collapsed with a fever and was bedridden for two months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969364Lynch2006186Arana2013315_355-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969364Lynch2006186Arana2013315-355">[352]</a></sup> Meanwhile, Tagle and the garrison of the city of <a href="/wiki/Callao" title="Callao">Callao</a> defected to the Royalists, who then took Lima.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969365–66Slattade_Grummond2003246Lynch2006187Arana2013317–18_356-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969365–66Slattade_Grummond2003246Lynch2006187Arana2013317–18-356">[353]</a></sup> In response, the Peruvian congress named Bolívar <a href="/wiki/Dictator" title="Dictator">dictator</a> of Peru on 10 February 1824. Bolívar moved to northern Peru in March and began assembling an army,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014398_352-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014398-352">[349]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch2006189–90_357-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch2006189–90-357">[354]</a></sup> for which he increasingly demanded additional men and money from Santander, straining their relationship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969368,_370Lynch2006189–90_358-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969368,_370Lynch2006189–90-358">[355]</a></sup> In May 1824, after learning of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ola%C3%B1eta%27s_rebellion&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Olañeta's rebellion (page does not exist)">a rebellion</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rebeli%C3%B3n_de_Ola%C3%B1eta" title="es:Rebelión de Olañeta">es</a>]</span> against the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viceroy_of_Peru" title="Viceroy of Peru">Viceroy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_la_Serna,_1st_Count_of_the_Andes" title="José de la Serna, 1st Count of the Andes">José de la Serna</a>, by conservative Royalist <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Antonio_Ola%C3%B1eta" title="Pedro Antonio Olañeta">Pedro Antonio Olañeta</a>, Bolívar began advancing in Peru,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969372Slattade_Grummond2003247Lynch2006191Arana2013320_359-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969372Slattade_Grummond2003247Lynch2006191Arana2013320-359">[356]</a></sup> and defeated Canterac at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Jun%C3%ADn" title="Battle of Junín">Battle of Junín</a> on 6 August.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969374–75Slattade_Grummond2003249–50Lynch2006192–93Langley200988Arana2013326–28_360-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969374–75Slattade_Grummond2003249–50Lynch2006192–93Langley200988Arana2013326–28-360">[357]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014402_361-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014402-361">[358]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Capitulaci%C3%B3n_de_Ayacucho1.jpg"><img alt="Painting depicting the Ayacucho capitulation" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2879" data-file-width="3833" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Capitulaci%C3%B3n_de_Ayacucho1.jpg/220px-Capitulaci%C3%B3n_de_Ayacucho1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Capitulaci%C3%B3n_de_Ayacucho1.jpg/330px-Capitulaci%C3%B3n_de_Ayacucho1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Capitulaci%C3%B3n_de_Ayacucho1.jpg/440px-Capitulaci%C3%B3n_de_Ayacucho1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Capitulaci%C3%B3n_de_Ayacucho1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Antonio_Jos%C3%A9_de_Sucre" title="Antonio José de Sucre">Antonio José de Sucre</a> accepting <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ayacucho_capitulation&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ayacucho capitulation (page does not exist)">the surrender</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capitulaci%C3%B3n_de_Ayacucho" title="es:Capitulación de Ayacucho">es</a>]</span> of <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_Canterac" title="José de Canterac">José de Canterac</a></div></div></div>
<p>Choosing to ignore Olañeta, La Serna ordered his forces to concentrate at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuzco" title="Cuzco">Cuzco</a> to face Bolívar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014402_361-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014402-361">[358]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969375Slattade_Grummond2003250_362-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969375Slattade_Grummond2003250-362">[359]</a></sup> Heavy rainfall in September halted Bolívar's advance,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969376Arana2013329_363-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969376Arana2013329-363">[360]</a></sup> and on 6 October he gave command of the army to Sucre and moved to <a href="/wiki/Huancayo" title="Huancayo">Huancayo</a> to manage political affairs. On 24 October, Bolívar received a letter from Santander informing him that because he had accepted the dictatorship of Peru, he had been stripped by the Colombian congress of his military and civil authority in favor of Sucre and Santander, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969376Slattade_Grummond2003251Lynch2006193Arana2013329_364-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969376Slattade_Grummond2003251Lynch2006193Arana2013329-364">[361]</a></sup> Although indignant and resentful of Santander, Bolívar wrote to him on 10 November to communicate his acquiescence <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003252Lynch2006193_365-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003252Lynch2006193-365">[362]</a></sup> and reoccupied Lima on 5 December 1824.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003252Arana2013331_366-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003252Arana2013331-366">[363]</a></sup> On 9 December, Sucre decisively defeated La Serna's Royalists at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ayacucho" title="Battle of Ayacucho">Battle of Ayacucho</a> and accepted <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ayacucho_capitulation&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ayacucho capitulation (page does not exist)">the surrender</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capitulaci%C3%B3n_de_Ayacucho" title="es:Capitulación de Ayacucho">es</a>]</span> of all Royalist forces in Peru. The Royalist garrison of Callao and Olañeta ignored the surrender. Shortly after arriving in Lima, Bolívar began <a href="/wiki/Second_siege_of_Callao" title="Second siege of Callao">a siege of Callao</a> that lasted until January 1826,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969378–79,_383Slattade_Grummond2003252–56Lynch2006194–95Arana2013331–35_367-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969378–79,_383Slattade_Grummond2003252–56Lynch2006194–95Arana2013331–35-367">[364]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014402–05_368-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014402–05-368">[365]</a></sup> and sent Sucre into Upper Peru to eliminate Olañeta, which he accomplished in April 1825.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014404–05_369-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFarlane2014404–05-369">[366]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="Final_years.2C_1825.E2.80.931830"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Final_years,_1825–1830">Final years, 1825–1830</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Final years, 1825–1830">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In early 1825, Bolívar resigned from his offices in Colombia and Peru, but neither nation's congress accepted his resignation; on 10 February 1825, the Peruvian congress extended his dictatorship for another year. Accepting the extension,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969381–82Slattade_Grummond2003256–57Lynch2006194–95Arana2013339_370-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969381–82Slattade_Grummond2003256–57Lynch2006194–95Arana2013339-370">[367]</a></sup> Bolívar settled into governing Peru and passing reforms that were largely not carried out, such as a school system based on the principles of English educator <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Lancaster" title="Joseph Lancaster">Joseph Lancaster</a> and managed by Simón Rodríguez.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch2006195–96Arana2013342–43_371-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch2006195–96Arana2013342–43-371">[368]</a></sup> In April 1825, Bolívar began a tour of southern Peru that took him to the cities of <a href="/wiki/Arequipa" title="Arequipa">Arequipa</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuzco" title="Cuzco">Cuzco</a> by August.
