As Bolívar approached Upper Peru, a congress gathered in the city of Chuquisaca (now <a href="/wiki/Sucre" title="Sucre">Sucre</a>); on 6 August, it <a href="/wiki/Bolivian_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Bolivian Declaration of Independence">declared the region's independence</a> as the new nation of <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a>, named Bolívar as <a href="/wiki/President_of_Bolivia" title="President of Bolivia">President of Bolivia</a>, and asked him to write a constitution. He accepted these appointments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969386–88Slattade_Grummond2003257Lynch2006195–96,_199Arana2013343–46_372-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969386–88Slattade_Grummond2003257Lynch2006195–96,_199Arana2013343–46-372">[369]</a></sup> Bolívar arrived in <a href="/wiki/Potos%C3%AD" title="Potosí">Potosí</a> on 5 October and met with two Argentine agents, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Mar%C3%ADa_de_Alvear" title="Carlos María de Alvear">Carlos María de Alvear</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Miguel_D%C3%ADaz_V%C3%A9lez" title="José Miguel Díaz Vélez">José Miguel Díaz Vélez</a>, who tried without success to convince him to intervene in the <a href="/wiki/Cisplatine_War" title="Cisplatine War">Cisplatine War</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Brazil" title="Empire of Brazil">Empire of Brazil</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969388–90Slattade_Grummond2003257Lynch2006200_373-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969388–90Slattade_Grummond2003257Lynch2006200-373">[370]</a></sup>
</p><p>From Potosí, Bolívar traveled to Chuquisaca, where he promised the Bolivian congress that he would have a constitution ready by the body's next meeting in May 1826. On 1 January 1826, he left Sucre to govern Bolivia and departed for Peru.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969391–92Slattade_Grummond2003261–62Lynch2006201_374-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969391–92Slattade_Grummond2003261–62Lynch2006201-374">[371]</a></sup> He arrived in Lima on 10 February 1826 and then dispatched his draft of the Bolivian constitution to Sucre on 12 May.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch2006201Arana2013348,_350_375-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch2006201Arana2013348,_350-375">[372]</a></sup> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Constitution_of_Bolivia_(1826)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Constitution of Bolivia (1826) (page does not exist)">This constitution</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constituci%C3%B3n_Pol%C3%ADtica_de_Bolivia_de_1826" title="es:Constitución Política de Bolivia de 1826">es</a>]</span>, ratified by the Bolivian congress in July 1826<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969394_376-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969394-376">[373]</a></sup> and widely distributed through the Atlantic world,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch2006203Arana2013351_377-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch2006203Arana2013351-377">[374]</a></sup> was controversial because of its abolition of slavery and provision for a <a href="/wiki/President_for_life" title="President for life">president for life</a> who chose their successor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969393–96Lynch2006202–04Arana2013350–51_378-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969393–96Lynch2006202–04Arana2013350–51-378">[375]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Death_and_burial">Death and burial</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Death and burial">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Muerte_de_Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="666" data-file-width="850" decoding="async" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Muerte_de_Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar.png/220px-Muerte_de_Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Muerte_de_Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar.png/330px-Muerte_de_Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Muerte_de_Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar.png/440px-Muerte_de_Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Muerte_de_Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bolívar's death, by Venezuelan painter <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Herrera_Toro" title="Antonio Herrera Toro">Antonio Herrera Toro</a></div></div></div>
<p>Bolívar resigned the presidency on 27 April 1830, intending to leave the country for exile in Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArana2013435_379-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArana2013435-379">[376]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 17 December 1830, at the age of 47, Simón Bolívar died of tuberculosis<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEConn20201_380-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEConn20201-380">[377]</a></sup> in the <a href="/wiki/Quinta_de_San_Pedro_Alejandrino" title="Quinta de San Pedro Alejandrino">Quinta de San Pedro Alejandrino</a> in Santa Marta.
</p><p>Bolívar's remains were buried in the cathedral of Santa Marta. Twelve years later, in 1842, at the request of President José Antonio Páez, they were moved from Santa Marta to Caracas, where they were buried in the Caracas Cathedral together with the remains of his wife and parents. In 1876, he was moved to a monument set up for his interment at the <a href="/wiki/National_Pantheon_of_Venezuela" title="National Pantheon of Venezuela">National Pantheon of Venezuela</a>. The <i>Quinta</i> near Santa Marta has been preserved as a museum with numerous references to his life. In 2010, symbolic remains of Manuela Sáenz, were also interred in Venezuela's National Pantheon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-381"><a href="#cite_note-381">[378]</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2008, then-<a href="/wiki/President_of_Venezuela" title="President of Venezuela">President of Venezuela</a> <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Ch%C3%A1vez" title="Hugo Chávez">Hugo Chávez</a> set up a commission<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-382"><a href="#cite_note-382">[379]</a></sup> to investigate theories that Bolívar was the victim of an assassination. On several occasions, Chávez claimed that Bolívar was in fact poisoned by "New Granada traitors".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-COHAforum_383-0"><a href="#cite_note-COHAforum-383">[380]</a></sup> In April 2010, infectious diseases specialist Paul Auwaerter studied records of Bolívar's symptoms and concluded that he might have suffered from chronic <a href="/wiki/Arsenic_poisoning" title="Arsenic poisoning">arsenic poisoning</a>, but that both <a href="/wiki/Acute_toxicity" title="Acute toxicity">acute</a> poisoning and murder were unlikely.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2010PAresearch_384-0"><a href="#cite_note-2010PAresearch-384">[381]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Telegraph_Allen_7_May_2010_385-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Telegraph_Allen_7_May_2010-385">[382]</a></sup> Later on, in July 2010, Bolívar's body was ordered to be exhumed to advance the investigations;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-msnbc_James_16_July_2010_386-0"><a href="#cite_note-msnbc_James_16_July_2010-386">[383]</a></sup> however, in July 2011, international forensics experts released their report, claiming there was no proof of poisoning or any other unnatural cause of death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-387"><a href="#cite_note-387">[384]</a></sup>
</p>

<ul><li><img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="360" data-file-width="400" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/P_history.svg/16px-P_history.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/P_history.svg/24px-P_history.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/P_history.svg/32px-P_history.svg.png 2x" width="16"/> <a href="/wiki/Portal:History" title="Portal:History">History portal</a></li>
<li><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yellow_flag_waving.svg"><img alt="icon" class="noviewer" data-file-height="268" data-file-width="249" decoding="async" height="16" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Yellow_flag_waving.svg/30px-Yellow_flag_waving.svg.png 2x" width="15"/></a> <a href="/wiki/Portal:Liberalism" title="Portal:Liberalism">Liberalism portal</a></li></ul></td></tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1063604349">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar a>span,.mw-parser-output .navbar a>abbr{text-decoration:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}</style><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Radicalism_sidebar" title="Template:Radicalism sidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Radicalism_sidebar" title="Template talk:Radicalism sidebar"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Radicalism_sidebar&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Bolívar was an admirer of both the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a> and the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArana201335,_52–53_388-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArana201335,_52–53-388">[385]</a></sup> While he was an admirer of U.S. independence, he did not believe that its governmental system could work in Latin America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBushnellLangley2008_389-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBushnellLangley2008-389">[386]</a></sup> Thus, he claimed that the governance of heterogeneous societies like Venezuela "will require a firm hand".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBushnellLangley2008100_390-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBushnellLangley2008100-390">[387]</a></sup> He felt that the U.S. had been established in land especially fertile for democracy. By contrast, he referred to Spanish America as having been subject to the "triple yoke of ignorance, tyranny, and vice".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArana2013224_391-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArana2013224-391">[388]</a></sup> If a republic could be established in such a land, in his mind, it would have to make some concessions in terms of liberty. This is shown when Bolívar blamed the fall of the <a href="/wiki/First_Republic_of_Venezuela" title="First Republic of Venezuela">first republic</a> on his subordinates trying to imitate "some ethereal republic" and in the process, not paying attention to the gritty political reality of South America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBushnellLangley2008136_392-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBushnellLangley2008136-392">[389]</a></sup>
</p><p>Bolívar was an avid reader, particularly of French <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enlightenment_philosophy" title="Enlightenment philosophy">Enlightenment philosophy</a>. Among his favorite authors were <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Hobbes" title="Thomas Hobbes">Thomas Hobbes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baruch_Spinoza" title="Baruch Spinoza">Baruch Spinoza</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Baron_d%27Holbach" title="Baron d'Holbach">Baron d'Holbach</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Hume" title="David Hume">David Hume</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montesquieu" title="Montesquieu">Montesquieu</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jean-Jacques_Rousseau" title="Jean-Jacques Rousseau">Jean-Jacques Rousseau</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200313_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200313-22">[21]</a></sup> Among the books accompanying him as he traveled were <a href="/wiki/Adam_Smith" title="Adam Smith">Adam Smith</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wealth_of_Nations" title="The Wealth of Nations">The Wealth of Nations</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Voltaire" title="Voltaire">Voltaire</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Letters_on_the_English" title="Letters on the English">Letters</a></i> and, when he was writing the Bolivian constitution, Montesquieu's <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Spirit_of_the_Laws" title="The Spirit of the Laws">The Spirit of the Laws</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch200633_393-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch200633-393">[390]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_places_and_things_named_after_Sim%C3%B3n_Bolivar" title="List of places and things named after Simón Bolivar">List of places and things named after Simón Bolivar</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EstatuaDelLibertadorEnLaPlazaBolivar2004-6.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/EstatuaDelLibertadorEnLaPlazaBolivar2004-6.jpg/200px-EstatuaDelLibertadorEnLaPlazaBolivar2004-6.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/EstatuaDelLibertadorEnLaPlazaBolivar2004-6.jpg/300px-EstatuaDelLibertadorEnLaPlazaBolivar2004-6.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/EstatuaDelLibertadorEnLaPlazaBolivar2004-6.jpg/400px-EstatuaDelLibertadorEnLaPlazaBolivar2004-6.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EstatuaDelLibertadorEnLaPlazaBolivar2004-6.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Plaza Bolívar, <a href="/wiki/Caracas" title="Caracas">Caracas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a></div></div></div>
<p>Due to the historical relevance of Bolívar as a key element during the process of independence in <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_America" title="Hispanic America">Hispanic America</a>, his memory has been strongly attached to sentiments of nationalism and patriotism, being a recurrent theme of rhetoric in politics.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Militarism#Venezuela" title="Militarism">In Venezuela, Bolívar left behind a militarist legacy</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-REVspec_394-0"><a href="#cite_note-REVspec-394">[391]</a></sup> with multiple governments utilizing the memory, image and written legacy of Bolívar as important parts of their political messages and propaganda.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CARRERA_395-0"><a href="#cite_note-CARRERA-395">[392]</a></sup> Bolívar disapproved of the excesses of "party spirit" and "factions", which led to an anti-political environment in Venezuela.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BLOCKcom_396-0"><a href="#cite_note-BLOCKcom-396">[393]</a></sup> For much of the 1800s, Venezuela was ruled by <i>caudillos</i>, with six rebellions occurring to take control of Venezuela between 1892 and 1900 alone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BLOCKcom_396-1"><a href="#cite_note-BLOCKcom-396">[393]</a></sup> The militarist legacy was then used by the nationalist dictatorship of <a href="/wiki/Marcos_P%C3%A9rez_Jim%C3%A9nez" title="Marcos Pérez Jiménez">Marcos Pérez Jiménez</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CARRERA_395-1"><a href="#cite_note-CARRERA-395">[392]</a></sup> and more recently the socialist <a href="/wiki/Bolivarian_Revolution" title="Bolivarian Revolution">political movement</a> led by Hugo Chávez.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Martin_VenezuelAnalysis_397-0"><a href="#cite_note-Martin_VenezuelAnalysis-397">[394]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (June 2022)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p><span class="anchor" id="Monuments_and_physical_legacy"></span>The nations of <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Bolivarian Republic of Venezuela</a>, and their respective currencies (the <a href="/wiki/Bolivian_boliviano" title="Bolivian boliviano">Bolivian boliviano</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Venezuelan_bol%C3%ADvar" title="Venezuelan bolívar">Venezuelan bolívar</a>), are all named after Bolívar. Most cities and towns in Colombia and Venezuela are built around a main square known as <a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Plaza_Bol%C3%ADvar_(disambiguation)" title="Plaza Bolívar (disambiguation)">Plaza Bolívar</a>, as is Bogotá.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-398"><a href="#cite_note-398">[395]</a></sup> His birthday is a <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Venezuela" title="Public holidays in Venezuela">public holiday in Venezuela</a> and <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Bolivia" title="Public holidays in Bolivia">Bolivia</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Several cities in Spain, especially in the <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(autonomous_community)" title="Basque Country (autonomous community)">Basque Country</a>, have constructed monuments to Bolívar, including a large monument in Bilbao<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-399"><a href="#cite_note-399">[396]</a></sup> and a comprehensive Venezuelan government-funded museum in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cenarruza-Puebla_de_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Cenarruza-Puebla de Bolívar">Cenarruza-Puebla de Bolívar</a>, his ancestral hometown.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-400"><a href="#cite_note-400">[397]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-3">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In isolation, <i>Simón</i> is pronounced as Spanish <small></small><span class="IPA" lang="es-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[siˈmon]</a></span>, and that is the pronunciation in the recording.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-121"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-121">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Biographers disagree on the exact date Miranda arrived in Venezuela in December 1810. Arana says 10 December,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArana201395_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArana201395-116">[115]</a></sup> Lynch says 11 December,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch200654_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch200654-117">[116]</a></sup> Masur and Langley say 12 December,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur196985_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur196985-118">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELangley200932_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELangley200932-119">[118]</a></sup> Slatta and de Grummond say 13 December.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200342_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond200342-120">[119]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-233"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-233">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Masur, Langley, and Arana state that Bolívar issued his proclamation of emancipation in early June.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasur1969197Langley200960Arana2013186_231-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasur1969197Langley200960Arana2013186-231">[229]</a></sup> Slatta, de Grummond, and Lynch state that it was issued a month later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003142Lynch2006100_232-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlattade_Grummond2003142Lynch2006100-232">[230]</a></sup></span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Further_reading">Further reading</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Further reading">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li>Bushnell, David. <i><a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/bolivarmanimage" rel="nofollow">The Liberator, Simón Bolívar: Man and Image</a></i>. New York: Alfred A. Knopf, 1970.</li>
<li>Bushnell, David and Macaulay, Neill. <i>The Emergence of Latin America in the Nineteenth Century</i> (Second edition). Oxford and New York: Oxford University Press, 1994. <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-19-508402-3" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-19-508402-3">978-0-19-508402-3</a></li>
<li>Gómez Martínez, José Luis. <a class="external text" href="http://www.ensayistas.org/jlgomez/estudios/bolivar.htm" rel="nofollow">"La encrucijada del cambio: Simón Bolívar entre dos paradigmas (una reflexión ante la encrucijada postindustrial)"</a>. <i>Cuadernos Americanos</i> 104 (2004): 11–32.</li>
<li>Lacroix, Luis Perú de. <i>Diario de Bucaramanga</i>. Caracas: Ministerio del Poder Popular para la Comunicación y la Información, 2009.</li>
<li>Lynch, John. <i>Simón Bolívar and the Age of Revolution</i>. London: University of London Institute of Latin American Studies, 1983. <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-901145-54-3" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-901145-54-3">978-0-901145-54-3</a></li>

New York: D. Appleton &amp; Co., 1858.</li>
<li>Racine, Karen. "Simón Bolívar and friends: Recent biographies of independence figures in Colombia and Venezuela" <i>History Compass</i> 18#3 (Feb 2020) <a class="external free" href="https://doi.org/10.1111/hic3.12608" rel="nofollow">https://doi.org/10.1111/hic3.12608</a></li></ul>
